Takeover of Gubeikou Postponed

｜Temporarily Postponed to March 4｜

Reasons Being:

Japanese Troop Rotation Not Yet Completed

Addresses of Various Agencies Undetermined

Yin Rugeng Returns to Beiping with Liu Youxun and Huo Shi

(Beiping) After Yin Rugeng met with Matsui in Gubeikou on the 26th, due to the incomplete troop rotation between the Ogawa Regiment of the 8th Division of the Japanese Army and the Nagami Regiment of the 7th Division, and the undetermined addresses of agencies such as the Sasaki Bureau and the Public Security Bureau, it was decided to postpone the takeover to March 4th. There are currently over two hundred Japanese troops stationed in Gubeikou, more than eighty puppet border police, and eight or nine Japanese military police. A puppet border police office is also located at the foot of Nantianguan slope. Inspections of passersby are very strict. Yin Rugeng returned to Beiping tonight with Liu Youxun and Huo Shi, and will go again on the 3rd to handle the matter. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Tianjin) Yin Rugeng left Gubeikou this afternoon and arrived in Beiping this evening. Due to the Japanese agencies not being withdrawn from Gubeikou, the takeover is postponed to March 4th. Japanese representative Matsui also returned to Chengde on the 28th and will return to Gubeikou on the 4th. Except for the two eastern passes of the five small passes nearby where Japanese troops are stationed, the rest have been recovered by us. At Nantianguan Gubeikou, pedestrians are inspected very strictly after 8 PM. The troop rotation between the 8th and 7th Divisions of the Japanese Army should be completed within a week. The thirty members of the War Zone Security Team transferred by us are temporarily stationed in Shixia Town and will be sent to Gubeikou after the takeover. When Yin Rugeng arrived, the public welcomed him with lanterns and dragon dances. A group of Chinese traitors in Gubeikou agitated the Japanese to oppose our takeover, so the Japanese side also seemed hesitant. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Beiping) According to a phone call from Miyun, Yin Rugeng secretly went to Chengde on the 26th to visit Matsui, but did not meet him. He returned to Gubeikou on the 27th and returned to Beiping in the afternoon. The postponement of the takeover of Gubeikou was originally due to the one-day enthronement of the Japanese puppet government, and there were no responsible Japanese personnel to handle it. The takeover on March 4th is also just a verbal agreement, and it is still difficult to predict whether it can be handled as scheduled. Currently, only Guan Qinghua, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, and two attendants are left in Gubeikou to negotiate everything. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Guangzhou) Gubeikou was not returned to China this morning. The Japanese military authorities requested a postponement of the handover ceremony because the military barracks were not yet completed, so it has been postponed to March 4th. (Reuters Telegram, 28th)

Fujian Provincial Government Cables Various Counties, Setting a Deadline for Eliminating Opium Seedlings

(Fuzhou) The Provincial Government cabled various counties, setting a deadline of twenty days to eliminate opium seedlings, and requiring the county magistrate to be responsible for reporting. Personnel will be sent to investigate. If there is any falsehood, severe punishment will be imposed immediately upon discovery. (Special Telegram, 28th)

The 7th Route Army Has Been Organized

Transferred to Henan for Training by Liu Zhi

(Nanjing) Military News: The former 19th Route Army has been reorganized by order of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek by Wei Lihuang into the 7th Route Army, comprising four divisions with three regiments each. The organization is now complete. The division and regimental commanders will be determined by the military authorities, and fixed numbers will be assigned. The Ministry of Military Affairs will submit a formal appointment in the coming days. The commanders are: 49th Division Commander Wu Chengren, 60th Division Commander Chen Pei, 61st Division Commander Yang Bufei, and 78th Division Commander Wen Chaoji. All divisions have now been transferred to Henan for training by Liu Zhi, and will be assigned other tasks after three months. (Central News Agency Telegram, 28th)

Central Government Decides to Approve Silver Agreement

The Issue of the United States Raising Silver Prices

To be Properly Addressed by the Executive Yuan

(Nanjing) In addition to resolving to approve the Silver Agreement, the Central Political Council on the 28th also made specific decisions on stabilizing silver prices and preventing the export of raw silver. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Nanjing) Regarding the Silver Agreement, the Central Political Council held a review meeting on the 27th. It was generally agreed that the effect of the agreement was to stabilize silver prices and seek international exchange stability, and that the government should approve joining. As for the US raising silver prices, this is another issue, and the Executive Yuan should entrust proper countermeasures to effectively prevent it. A review opinion was drafted and submitted by the Standing Committee for discussion at the Central Political Council on the 28th. After a long period of research, it was decided to pass it according to the review opinion and submit it to the Legislative Yuan for review. The Legislative Yuan meeting in two days can bring it up for discussion. (Central News Agency Telegram, 28th)

(Nanjing) Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi took the train to Shanghai on the night of the 20th. It is said that after careful research by various committees at the review meeting on the 27th regarding the Silver Agreement, opinions were signed and submitted for discussion at the Central Political Council on the 28th, and it has been resolved to pass it and submit it to the Legislative Yuan for review. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Nanjing) A certain Central Committee member said that the Silver Agreement was approved by the Central Political Council on the 28th. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Fierce Fighting in Jiangle

Chiang Orders Recovery of County Seat in Three Days

The Bandit Suppression Army in Western Fujian Presses on Changting

(Fuzhou) Military News: The fighting in Jiangle is fierce. Chairman Chiang cabled General Sun to recover the county seat of Jiangle County within three days. The bandits of Gaotan Shuinan under Jiang were defeated by the 264th Route Army on the 27th. The large bandit suppression army in western Fujian has now made contact with the various armies in northern Fujian and is pressing on Changting. Wei Lihuang will go to Xiamen today to meet Chiang Ting-wen and then go to Longyan to establish the forward headquarters. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Fuzhou) The two divisions of Leng Xin and Lu Xingbang completely recovered Sha County on the 25th. The pseudo-Third Army Corps fled to Xiamao and was severely attacked by Sun Yuanliang's division, suffering heavy casualties. They fled westward to Jiangle. Now Lu's division is stationed in Shacheng, and Sun's and Leng's divisions are pursuing and suppressing them in different directions. The remaining bandits in Jiangle, Yong'an and other places can be cleared soon. (Special Telegram, 27th)

Japanese Troops Stationed in Tianjin Conduct Field Maneuvers of Offense and Defense

(Tianjin) The Japanese troops stationed in Tianjin have reached an agreement with the BeiNing Railway for vehicles. It is scheduled that the commander Nakamura will lead troops at 4 AM on the 1st to conduct field maneuvers of offense and defense in Duliu River Liangwangzhuang, Jinghai County, and other places for four days and camp on the spot. During the maneuvers, they will be divided into offensive and defensive teams. Armored vehicles and tanks participating have already been sent. (Special Telegram, 28th)

British Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen to Present Credentials on the 6th

(Nanjing) The newly appointed British Ambassador to China, Knatchbull-Hugessen (the British Embassy has changed the Chinese translation of his name as above because the original translation, Kai Du Gan, was deemed inappropriate), arrived in Shanghai on the 26th of last month with his wife and three daughters aboard the SS Chitral. Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen is scheduled to take the night train to Nanjing at 11 PM on the 2nd. The British Consul-General in Nanjing, Braund, has prepared the reception room in front of the consulate for Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen to stay in and has requested a date to meet with Chairman Lin. Chairman Lin approved the date of 11 AM on the morning of March 6th for Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen to present his credentials on the evening of the 28th. All the etiquette has been ordered to be prepared by the Civil Affairs Department in conjunction with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Fu Zuoyi and Fu Zhankui Leave Beiping for Suiyuan Together

Men Bingyue, Zhang Xuanze, and Wang Zhongquan Accompany Them

Military Expenses for Shanxi-Suiyuan Army Have Been Received

Ji Hu and Pang Again Telegraph to Sun

Military Council Also Adds Admonition

(Beiping) Fu Zuoyi, Fu Zhankui, Men Bingyue, and senior staff officers of the sub-committee Zhang Xuanze and Wang Zhongquan, took the same car to Suiyuan at 4:40 PM on the 28th. Fu said, "I asked Minister He about various matters in Beiping, and everything is roughly in order. The military expenses have been received, including the costs of mobilization and transportation. I will arrive in Suiyuan tomorrow and, after sorting out military and political matters, I will go to the front to supervise everything." Although the sub-committee is taking active military action against Sun's troops, it has not completely abandoned the intention of a peaceful resolution. If Sun can fulfill his previous promise and leave the army, everything can still be resolved peacefully. Otherwise, a military sanction will be decided. I will stay in Suiyuan for about three or four days and then depart. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Beiping) Ji Yiqiao, Hu Yukun, and Pang Bingxun telegraphed Sun on the 28th, saying, "To Commander Sun Dianying of Dengkou, upon reading your telegram, we deeply admire your vision and feelings and appreciate them deeply. We have presented your intentions to Mr. He in person. He has appointed three brothers, Dang Xingqiao, Wang Zhongquan, and Zhang Xuanze, to go today. All the details have been entrusted to Brother Xingqiao to convey. You have always put the country first and based your actions on the will of the people, taking the overall situation into consideration and never lagging behind. This time, you should be able to resolve it thoroughly. Knowing your concerns, we respectfully inform you in advance. Ji Yiqiao, Hu Yukun, and Pang Bingxun kowtow with respect. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Beiping) The various members of the Military Council had previously jointly telegraphed Sun, urging him to leave the army early. Sun replied to the members on the 23rd, expressing his agreement. It was reported at the sub-committee's routine meeting this morning. During the meeting, it was decided that the entire group would again jointly telegraph Sun, asking him to leave the army as soon as possible. The Council will be responsible for guaranteeing his life safety and hopes that he will leave the army soon. The place of residence will be at his own discretion. The telegram has been sent. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Beiping) Fu has received the military expenses for the Shanxi-Suiyuan army. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Fu Zhankui Discusses the Mission of This Trip

(Beiping) Fu Zhankui said, "I will first go to Baotou with Zhang Xuanze and Wang Zhongquan, and then take a car to the front. The meeting place with Sun is around Dengkou. Because it is quite inconvenient to negotiate by telegram, we have not decided on a specific location. The only task of this trip is to ask Sun whether he sincerely intends to leave the army. If he is sincere, we will continue to discuss all the arrangements for the aftermath. Otherwise, I will return to Beiping to report. Hu Jiesan was unable to travel with us due to some matters." (Special Telegram, 28th)

Shanxi Army Advances Toward Sun's Troops

(Beiping) A telegram from Guihua said that Wang Jingguo's troops have been completely assembled. He ordered the two brigades of Wang Tingying and Tian Shumei to start advancing. Wang received a telegram from Wang Tingying on the 26th, stating that his brigade was advancing according to the original plan. Xu Zizhen's regiment arrived near Huangka Yihe at noon on the 25th and discovered more than twenty soldiers and cavalry from Peng's brigade of the enemy army, who were entrenched there, attempting to resist stubbornly. Regiment Commander Xu led his troops to launch a fierce attack, firing artillery while leading the troops to attack and engage in a fierce battle. The enemy could not withstand the attack and fled southwest, and they are still pursuing them. Also, Zhao Shazhou's cavalry brigades and Wang's and Tian's brigades are also advancing fiercely in coordination. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Sun's Troops Dig Tunnels Against Ningyuan

(Beiping) Relevant sources received a telegram from Ningxia You: (1) Sun is still supervising the battle in the Xujiazhuang, Zhaogezhuang, and Baitai areas more than ten li north of Ningyuan and is attacking Ningyuan fiercely with artillery fire. The Ningyuan army bravely resisted the enemy and captured three armored vehicles. (2) Sun's army is based in various places outside the city of Pingluo, attacking and retreating from time to time. The trenches made by Sun's army have all been destroyed by the Ningyuan army. Also, Sun's army is currently digging tunnels against the city wall of Ningyuan, but the work is difficult due to the frozen soil. Sun also expressed his desire to capture Ningyuan quickly, as he can get an income of 6 million yuan every year. If Ningyuan is captured, he will not interfere with the political power and tax revenue rights. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Pang Says Mediation Has Come to an End

(Beiping) Pang Bingxun said that he, Hu, and Ji had persuaded Sun to leave the army and that he had agreed. After consulting with He, it was decided to send Fu Zhankui to meet with Sun. His task of mediation can be considered to have come to an end. At the same time, because he has been away from his defense area for a long time, he plans to return to his defense area within two or three days. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Yu Xuezhong Discusses the Aftermath of the Yutian Incident

(Beiping) Yu Xuezhong returned to Tianjin by special train at 3 PM on the 28th. According to him, the aftermath of the Yutian security team has been discussed and decided with Chairman Huang. A team of 1,000 people will be formed, and Han Dianbang has been selected as the captain. After Yin Rugeng completes the takeover of Gubeikou, he will go together to handle the matter of reorganization. However, the internal affairs of the team are complicated. Currently, they are still suppressing bandits, asking the provincial government for money, and disobeying the provincial government's orders, which is very strange. Also, each county in the war zone used to have ten districts, which was too large. A method has now been drafted to merge them in the field to reduce governance. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Tianjin) Chairman of Hebei Province, Yu Xuezhong, returned to Tianjin from Beiping at 6:30 PM this evening. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Routine Meeting of the Beiping Military Council

(Beiping) The Military Council held its 46th routine meeting at 10 AM on the 28th. The attendees included Xu Yongchang, Yu Xuezhong, Fu Zuoyi, Wan Fulin, Shang Zhen, Chiang Bo-cheng, Qin Dechun, Xiao Zhenying, Men Bingyue, Wei Yisan, Zou Zuohua, Hu Yukun, and Ji Yiqiao, among other twenty people. He Yingqin presided over the meeting, and the following matters were discussed: (1) Wan Fulin proposed a plan on how to regulate the purchase of official horses by various troops. It was resolved that before the official horses of each troop are prepared, those purchased by private individuals shall be supplied with feed by the public. (2) Liu Yifei had previously led the Vanguard Army to garrison Shangdumiao Baosaichang, and the grains used were levied from the local area. Now, they are requesting to be returned. It was resolved that the Chahar Provincial Government should investigate the amount of subsidies paid on its behalf and submit them to the meeting for review and issuance. (3) Other routine cases. After the meeting, a meeting of the officer examination committee above the rank of colonel was held to approve several cases of retaining the director of the Dagu Shipyard and promoting various officers. The meeting adjourned at 12 noon. (Central News Agency Telegram, 28th)

Huang Shouzhong's Guerrilla Unit in Chahar is Disbanded

(Beiping) Qin and Xiao are scheduled to return to Zhangjiakou on the afternoon of the 1st. It is rumored that Song is scheduled to come to Beiping from Shandong around the 7th and then transfer to Zhangjiakou. The military discipline of Huang Shouzhong's First Detachment of the Chahar Guerrilla has been lax. Song has dismissed him from his post and canceled his designation. Huang's unit has also been disbanded. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Puppet Organization Implements New Tariff System

(Tianjin) From March 1st, the puppet organization will implement a new tariff system on us and will set up customs checkpoints on the Great Wall line at Lengkou, Jielingkou, Yiyuan Kou, and Malanlue. For example, the import tax on coarse cloth, cattle, and sheep will all increase by one-third. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Chen and Chiang Conferred Secretly on Bandit Suppression

Chiang Waiting in Guangdong to Meet Li Zongren

Huang Hechun's Troops Transported to Shantou for Accommodation

Li Yangjing Decides to Convene a Joint Conference

(Hong Kong) Chiang Ting-wen is staying at Tuisiyuan. Chen Jitang went to the garden again on the morning of the 28th to meet with Chiang to discuss bandit suppression in secret. The security was extremely tight. Li Zongren is said to be coming to Guangdong in two days to meet with Chiang. Chiang said on the 28th that he came to Guangdong on the orders of Chairman Chiang to meet with Chen to discuss bandit suppression. After arriving in Guangdong, he consulted with various military and political leaders and has had considerable results. He plans to return to Xiamen by plane on the 2nd. The military affairs of the Eastern Route are now aimed at developing in the northwest. Because the main force of the bandits is gathered there, the bandit suppression troops of this route have begun to concentrate. After he arrives in Xiamen, he plans to fly to Jiangxi to meet with Chiang and report on his trip to Guangdong. The start of military affairs on the southeast and eastern routes should be decided when he meets with Chiang. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Hong Kong) Yang Dezhao arrived in Guangdong on the same plane with Chiang Ting-wen on the 27th. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Hong Kong) Li Yangjing decided to convene a joint conference of the Guangdong-Fujian border bandit suppression and pacification fronts after the Eastern District Pacification Conference closed. Huang Renhuan, Deng Longguang, Li Zhenliang, Zhang Ruigui, and others all participated. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Hong Kong) The Zhixingbu Political Council held a joint banquet for Chiang Ting-wen on the afternoon of the 28th. Chiang decided to stay in Guangdong for a few more days to wait to meet with Li Zongren. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Hong Kong) Li Yangjing and Lin Yunhai arrived in Lufeng on the 28th. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Hong Kong) After Huang Hechun's brigade was disarmed, they were transported to Shantou for accommodation and awaiting orders. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Xiamen) Chen Jitang sent Zeng Xisan, a senior staff officer of the Independent 3rd Division, to visit Li Yutang, the commander of the 3rd Division, to serve as a liaison between the Guangdong and Central armies. The Guangdong army is currently stationed in Shanghang, Wuping, and Yongding, heading towards southern Jiangxi. The Central army will take over the defense of Longyan, Zhangping, Ningyang, and Liancheng and can mobilize within a week. It is rumored that a certain Wen from the southwest committee is the director of the Post-War Relief Office in southern Fujian, but this is not the case. Currently, the militias Peng Tangzong are attacking Yongchun in two directions, one occupying Dabao and the other holding a standoff in Xiaohu. The fighting is very fierce. The 3rd Division of Zhangzhou has concentrated and can set out to Longyan in three days. There is no Central army in Longyan yet. After the Guangdong army withdraws, a part will be left behind, waiting for the 3rd Division to take over. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Guangzhou) Chiang Ting-wen arrived here yesterday by plane from Xiamen and today held long consultations on military matters with Chen Jitang. The leaders of Guangzhou welcomed Chiang very warmly, and the newspapers also wrote about it extensively. Although the nature of today's meeting has not been announced, it is generally believed that Chiang will discuss the military situation in southern Fujian and the anti-communist war in Jiangxi Province with the Guangdong authorities. According to Chiang's words, public order in Fujian Province is gradually recovering, and post-war reconstruction work is currently underway. The public views Chiang's arrival in Guangdong as extremely important, as it proves that the tense situation between Nanjing and Guangdong is gradually easing. (Reuters Telegram, 28th)

Political Commentary

The Return of Yuguan and Gubeikou

In late May of last year, China and Japan signed the Tanggu Truce Agreement. Our troops withdrew to the area west and south of the line connecting Yanqing and Lutai, while the Japanese army continued to occupy the war zone and did not immediately comply with the agreement to "return to the line of the Great Wall." After repeated negotiations by our side, Yuguan was handed over on February 9th of this year, and Gubeikou was scheduled to be handed over on February 28th. Yuguan had been occupied for one year and thirty-seven days from the time it fell to the time it was recovered. Gubeikou had also been occupied for more than eight months. There are no fewer than sixteen passes on the Great Wall, large and small. Among them, the Japanese have built barracks in five major passes such as Panjiakou, Lengkou, Jiumenkou, Yiyuan Kou, and Jielingkou, citing the instability of the bandit atmosphere as an excuse for refusing to withdraw at the same time, which is obviously inconsistent with the agreement. In the Yuguan area, in addition to the original Japanese troops stationed there according to the Boxer Protocol, the remaining troops have been moved, but the barracks outside the city south of the railway have been greatly expanded and can garrison more than a division. Before the move, they also threatened to return at any time. The Japanese army in Gubeikou also said that there were no suitable houses outside the pass and refused to withdraw immediately. Their intention was to build barracks in Qingshiliang outside the pass and move there after the construction was completed. Judging from their arrangements, they all have deep intentions. If there is an emergency, the Japanese troops in the two places are close at hand and can arrive in an instant. The so-called troop withdrawal is just deceiving people.

Looking at the actual situation of the recovery of the two places, it is even more difficult for us to be optimistic immediately. Not only have the puppet Manchukuo agencies such as post offices and customs not been eliminated quickly, but they also seem to be on equal footing with us. Even the administrative power and police power that are said to have been returned have been stripped away, which is not enough to say that the territory is intact. Our police stationed in Yuguan are still holding wooden sticks on guard, while the puppet police are fully armed and strutting through the city every day, which cannot but make people feel that the guest is taking over the role of the host. Although Tao Shangming has repeatedly negotiated this matter, the Japanese side only allows the Chinese police to be equipped with short swords and pistols and absolutely not to use large guns. The number of pistols is also limited to 50. It is feared that Japanese and Korean thugs will cause trouble in the area after the takeover, and fifty pistols are hardly enough to maintain public order and even less to prevent bandits. The Japanese side also requires that the number of police and security teams stationed by our side in Gubeikou and the number of guns be limited, intending not to exceed 500 people, and that the police on duty not carry guns. It is speculated that the Japanese side intends to limit our ability to maintain public order and indirectly cultivate bandits in order to leave room for them to interfere at any time. Moreover, it is said that Japanese thugs and Japanese military police in Yuguan are constantly entering and leaving the Public Security Bureau and the county government to investigate our measures. Although our side cannot bear the trouble, we cannot refuse. From all this, we can see a glimpse of the Japanese people's intentions. We should not be satisfied with the beauty of the handover.

Given the disparity in strength between China and Japan and the low credibility of the Japanese side, what can we do if the various passes of the Great Wall are captured by the enemy and not returned for a long time? Why would the Japanese be willing to show us favor and actually return Yuguan and Gubeikou? According to our observations, there are probably two reasons: First, to ease the anti-Japanese sentiment in various quarters; and second, to lure our country to negotiate with them on issues such as through traffic and postal services between inside and outside the Customs in order to de facto recognize the hatred of the puppet Manchukuo. Let us discuss them separately.

Since Japan occupied our four northeastern provinces, its policy toward China has obviously undergone a change. Before this, its purpose was primarily to encompass the resources and sovereignty of the Northeast. After this, it primarily aimed to seize the market inside the Customs. Now that the purpose of occupying the Northeast has been achieved, and the anti-Japanese wave among Chinese has gradually subsided, for the Japanese people, it is appropriate to avoid military action and cultivate the purchasing power of our market inside the Customs to be the tailwater of Japanese goods dumping. Moreover, Japan's international diplomacy has long fallen into a state of isolation and helplessness. If it does not make every effort to narrow the scope of its armed actions in China, it will inevitably promote a united front of all parties to deal with the common enemy, and Japan will be on the verge of danger. Guangtian, the new foreign minister, said in his speech on diplomatic policy, "China's rapid recovery of its security and prosperity is the sincere hope of the empire." Its intention is probably to open up a diplomatic outlet on the one hand and recover the Chinese market on the other. It is a true expression of its internal psychology to take a two-pronged approach and take care of everything.

The Japanese side is eager to resolve issues such as through traffic and postal services between inside and outside the Customs as soon as possible. In the past few months, it has repeatedly encouraged our side to directly negotiate with the puppet Manchukuo to make us de facto recognize the puppet state as the precursor to other countries recognizing it one by one. Fortunately, our side's attitude is firm, and although there was an initial contact, it eventually stopped. Recently, the Japanese side, because Yuguan and Gubeikou have been returned, believes that events such as through traffic and postal services can continue to be negotiated.

The main reasons for the Japanese side's handover of the two places are nothing more than the above. Now, we want to tell the national public: (1) Under the current environment, when negotiating the recovery of lost territory, it is in the interest of the authorities to seek perfection. However, various parties have already been skeptical of our signing of the Tanggu Truce Agreement. If the conditions originally stipulated in the agreement cannot be fulfilled by the Japanese people one by one, how can we comfort the hopes of our people? For the authorities, they should continue to work hard to demand that the Japanese people return all the passes of the Great Wall and strive to get rid of the restrictions on our administrative and police powers regarding the recovery of various places. (2) We should continue to adhere to our past attitude on events such as through traffic and postal services with the puppet Manchukuo to avoid the suspicion of de facto recognizing the puppet organization. Previously, it was reported that the Ministry of Finance planned to send personnel to inspect and proceed as appropriate. However, because public opinion indicated that this matter was similar to establishing customs duties on the border and its abuses were no different from through traffic and postal services, the matter was terminated. From now on, we hope that our authorities will continue to respect public opinion and consider diplomacy and not lose sight of the big picture because of small things. (3) When the contacts between the recovered passes and the interior are well strengthened, setting up long-distance telephones and opening up highways are particularly urgent. It is necessary to proceed as soon as possible without delay. (4) It should be recognized that the return of Yuguan and Gubeikou is the result of the Japanese side fulfilling the Tanggu Truce Agreement and changing its diplomatic policy toward China. We should never be complacent about it. Before the entire China-Japan issue is resolved, we should always hold on to the original intention of recovering the Northeast and strive to implement it.

Macau and Guangzhou to Conduct Aviation Business

(Guangzhou) According to today's Vanguard News Agency, Macau Chinese businessmen are currently planning to open aviation business between Macau, Guangzhou, and Hong Kong. It is said that the governments of Guangdong and Hong Kong have approved this proposal. After a suitable location for the airport is found, aircraft will be purchased. (Reuters Telegram, 28th)

Russian Troops Fire on Japanese Plane, Russo-Japanese Relations Worsen

Russian Planes Also Fly Over Korean Border Twice

Japan Calls Russian Government to Attention

Russian Cavalry Investigates Border Terrain

(Tokyo) Russo-Japanese relations have suddenly turned sour. News arrived in Tokyo this morning that Russian troops shot down a Japanese military aircraft on February 17th at the confluence of the Amur and Songhua Rivers. However, details of the incident vary. Some say that everyone on board was killed, while others say that there were no casualties. Another report suggests that it is unknown which country's people shot down the Japanese aircraft. The Ministry of the Army stated regarding this matter that it has not yet received an official report, but a ministry spokesman said that Russian planes flew over the Korean border twice, on February 23rd and 25th. (February 28th Reuters dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Foreign Ministry has now learned that the strange aircraft that flew over the northern Korean border on the 23rd was a Soviet Russian plane. Therefore, today it sent a telegram to Ambassador Ota, instructing him to call the Moscow government to serious attention. (February 28th, Dentsu dispatch)

(Tokyo) According to a telegram from the Hunchun Consulate to the Foreign Ministry, at 11:00 AM on the 24th, eight cavalrymen from Kropotkin suddenly crossed the border, invading Tiandaopaozi in "Manchukuo" and investigating the terrain in that area before leaving. Recently, with the arrival of strange planes and the invasion of cavalry, the actions of the Soviet side have been quite active, causing anxiety among the Korean people. (February 28th Dentsu dispatch)

(Tokyo) Recently, strange aircraft have frequently flown over Jilin and northern Korea. The Foreign Ministry telegraphed the Governor-General of Korea, requesting an investigation into the truth of the matter and an immediate report. According to their report today, at 3:30 AM on the 23rd, aircraft flew over Gyeongwon, Sinheung, Gyeongseong, Unggi, and Najin in Hamgyeongbuk-do. At 5:30 AM, they entered Hunchun County and flew towards the Soviet Union. At 3:00 PM on the 25th, an aircraft appeared over Liudaogou in "Manchukuo" on the opposite bank of Gyeongseong, and flew through Qidaogou and Badaogou towards the Soviet Union from Hedaogou. The Foreign Ministry plans to investigate further and, if the strange aircraft indeed belong to Soviet Russia, will lodge a protest. (February 28th Dentsu dispatch)

(Tokyo) According to an official military report, on February 23rd, Russian troops used machine guns to fire at a Japanese aircraft scouting near the confluence of the Amur and Songhua Rivers. The aircraft was participating in "bandit suppression" operations at the time. It is reported that the pilot only suffered minor injuries, and the fuselage had a bullet hole. It is also reported that a similar incident occurred on February 12th, but the aircraft was undamaged. (February 28th Reuters dispatch)

(Tokyo) Although the Foreign Ministry ordered the Japanese ambassador in Moscow to protest the Soviet Russian aircraft's actions of flying over the Korean border, the Ministry of the Army does not attach much importance to this matter. Furthermore, according to a spokesman for the Ministry of the Army speaking to a Reuters reporter, the Ministry of the Army also does not attach importance to the matter of Russian troops firing at the Japanese aircraft, because the soldiers operating the machine guns may have mistakenly thought that the Japanese aircraft had crossed the border and therefore opened fire. (February 28th Reuters dispatch)

Former British Fleet Commander Advocates Expanding the Navy

Treaty Allowances Do Not Meet British Needs

Should Shed All Restraints at Next Year's Conference

(London) Admiral Beatty (Commander-in-Chief of the British Fleet from 1916 to 1919) issued a statement today advocating for the expansion of the British Navy, saying, "The British Navy has already been reduced to a level where national security is threatened. The intention is simply to set an example on the issue of disarmament. The ratio granted to Britain by the London Naval Treaty is not at all suitable for Britain's needs. Therefore, when the naval conference convenes in 1935, we should shed all restraints." (February 27th Havas dispatch)

Our Military Delegation Departs Turkey for Russia

Istanbul: The Chinese military delegation, led by Yang Jie, president of the Nanjing Army Military Academy, departed for Moscow today after staying here for twelve days. While in Turkey, they were warmly received by Turkish President Kemal and other dignitaries. Yang told a Reuters reporter that he believes diplomatic relations between China and Turkey will be established soon. Yang and his delegation are currently studying military science in various European countries and are expected to arrive in England in early spring. (February 28th Reuters dispatch)

Little Entente Countries Prepare to Restore Relations with Russia

Turkish and Romanian Foreign Ministers to Accompany to Russian Capital

Istanbul: News today says that diplomatic officials from Turkey and Romania will soon accompany each other to Moscow to discuss the restoration of diplomatic relations between Soviet Russia and the Little Entente countries (i.e., Czechoslovakia, Romania, and Yugoslavia) with Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov. (February 28th Reuters dispatch)

Anglo-Japanese Conference Bleak

Both Sides Striving to Find a Way Out

(London) Representatives of the British and Japanese textile industries resumed negotiations today, but after exchanging opinions, they adjourned the meeting until March 7th. The deadlock remains on the question of whether the scope of discussion should include the world market or be limited to the British and its colonial markets. (February 28th Reuters dispatch)

(London) According to reliable sources, the Anglo-Japanese textile negotiations have now reached a very complex stage. However, British representatives deny reports that the discussions have been suspended. It is reported that both sides will convene at the Ministry of Commerce and strive to find a way out. The Japanese delegation frequently contacts Tokyo, while the British representatives have held several secret meetings to discuss the points of contention. If the negotiations break down, calls for boycotting Japanese goods in the British market will likely intensify, and the matter may be handled through diplomatic channels. (February 28th Reuters dispatch)

Japanese House of Peers Urgent Interpellation of Education Minister Hatoyama

Prime Minister Saito Replied That He Will Deal with It Soon

Hatoyama Expressed Intent to Find a Good Solution

(Tokyo) Today's plenary session of the House of Peers began at 10:42 AM. First, Mr. Otsuka Koreshige addressed the chamber regarding

Then, listing various inauspicious events in education, he began his interpellation, saying,

Any one of these events is enough to impeach the responsibility of the Ministry of Education. We do not have the time to discuss each of these events in detail, because there are even more urgent issues at hand. We have read extremely severe and dishonorable criticisms of Education Minister Hatoyama in the newspapers. Moreover, according to Mr. Okamoto Ikki's speeches in the House of Representatives on February 8th and 15th, it is a regrettable thing that the Education Minister himself, in the position of an elder statesman of the academic world, was found at an inquiry. This is also regrettable for the Saito Cabinet. His Majesty the Emperor is extremely concerned about education. How should the Education Minister feel about this in his heart? If the Education Minister can clear away the doubts and make the situation clear to the education world, it would be something that the entire nation would eagerly desire. I hope that Prime Minister Saito will handle this matter decisively.

Prime Minister Saito answered,

Regarding the case of Education Minister Hatoyama, various rumors have been circulating, and the matter has become an issue in the House of Representatives. Even a special committee has been established. It is appropriate to wait until the results are clear before taking appropriate action.

At this time, Mr. Otsuka still wanted to pursue the matter, but due to the order of speaking, Mr. Nomura Tokushichi questioned him, saying,

I also agree with Mr. Otsuka's question. Please ask Education Minister Hatoyama to give a clear explanation.

Education Minister Hatoyama ascended the platform and answered with extreme caution, as follows:

I have not met Mr. Nomura in these past few years. I originally did not intend to say a word regarding Mr. Otsuka's speech. However, now that I have been moved by Mr. Nomura, I must make a brief statement. Recently, criticisms of me have been prevalent in society. I am deeply concerned that this will have a great impact on the education world. Therefore, I intend to approach this matter with a clear and calm mind and find a good solution. The meeting adjourned at 11:42 AM. (February 28th, Domei News Agency dispatch)

Number of Japanese Troops Mobilized Since the September 18th Incident

Total of 343,000 in the Army and Navy

(Tokyo) In the budget submitted to the Diet by the Japanese military, there is a huge sum for rewards for the September 18th Incident and the Shanghai Incident. The numbers shown are as follows:

(1) Ministry of the Army: 248,000 people

(A) Army soldiers dispatched: 168,000 people

(B) Army mobilization within the country: 80,000 people

(2) Ministry of the Navy: 95,000 people

(A) Navy personnel dispatched: 47,000 people

(B) Navy mobilization within the country: 58,000 people

The total number of Army and Navy personnel is 343,000. The Air Force is included. (February 28th, China United News Agency dispatch)

Japanese Emigrants to South America

141 Families Set Sail

Kobe: South America, especially Brazil, is a promising land of opportunity. A total of 141 families, numbering over 900 people, have been processed for emigration. Among them are 95 men and 409 women. They boarded the merchant ship Buwa Maru from Kobe at 4:00 PM on the 27th and set sail. Among them is Mr. Domoto Takehiro, a member of the Social Masses Party and a Fukuoka Prefectural Assembly member, as well as a Yawata City Council member, who also plans to stay in North and South America for about ten months to investigate the living conditions of Japanese residents in the Americas and to offer condolences. He also departed on the ship. (February 28th, Domei News Agency dispatch)

Impressions of a Former French Education Minister's Travels in the Far East

Lectures in China and Japan Did Not Involve Politics

Marseilles: French Senator Anatole de Monzie, former Minister of Education and initiator of the Cité Universitaire in Paris, was invited to give lectures in China and Japan last month. He recently returned to Marseilles aboard a French mail ship and issued a statement to our correspondent, recounting his lectures in Tokyo and Kyoto, saying, "My lectures in Japan did not involve politics in order to avoid causing disputes. I only expounded a noble concept, which is the mutual understanding of outstanding individuals from various countries to seek the cooperation of all nations. At present, the whole world is plagued by economic depression, and the cause of the depression is mostly due to misunderstandings and divisions among nations. To eliminate these misunderstandings and divisions requires the joint efforts of intellectuals from the East and the West. Japanese intellectuals warmly supported my proposal, which greatly moved me. After leaving Japan, I went to Beijing and Shanghai, where I was welcomed everywhere. I met with a large number of important Chinese officials. They are familiar with Western culture and all said that it is a pity that the Far East and the West have long been separated by misunderstandings. I then pointed out to them the contribution of the Cité Universitaire in Paris to bridging the feelings of students from various countries." (Note: The Cité Universitaire in Paris is located in the suburbs of Paris and has dormitories for students from various countries at the University of Paris.) "I am confident that the lectures I gave in China will have the same effect as in Japan." Anatole de Monzie is scheduled to depart from here for Paris tonight. (February 28th, Havas News Agency dispatch)

British Political Parties Dissatisfied with Current Cabinet Policies

(London) Opposition to Foreign Secretary Simon's strategy has ended, but unrest continues within the various political parties. The Liberal Party and the extreme Conservatives are extremely dissatisfied with Prime Minister MacDonald. Both sides are criticizing the Prime Minister's social policies and his attitude on the issue of disarmament, but for different reasons. (February 28th, Havas dispatch)

French Budget Bill Passed by Senate in its Entirety

Returned to the Chamber of Deputies for Reconsideration

New Cabinet Overcomes Current Difficulties

(Paris) The hope of new Prime Minister Doumergue that the budget bill for the current period would be passed by the Chamber of Deputies and the Senate before March 1st has now been realized. After being passed by the Chamber of Deputies, the budget bill was submitted to the Senate today, where it was passed by a large majority of 296 votes to 13. However, it was accompanied by several amendments that will be sent back to the Chamber of Deputies for discussion. These amendments do not seem to pose any difficulties. The speedy passage of this bill was due to the fact that both houses approved the entire vote without voting on each item. Doumergue has thus overcome a major current difficulty. The reason why previous cabinets collapsed shortly after being formed was their failure to overcome this difficulty. (February 27th, Reuters dispatch)

(Paris) The Senate today approved the government's full power to cut political expenses by order before June 30th by a vote of 277 to 19. Prime Minister Doumergue stated that he would resign if he did not obtain full power, hence the Senate's vote. (February 27th, Reuters dispatch)

Startling New Discoveries in French Swindle Case Continue

Involving Many Important Political Figures

Hubert Pierlot Also Among Those Implicated

Investigative Committee Has Begun Thorough Investigation

Supreme Court Justice Dismissed

(Paris) The waves of the French Stavisky scandal have now resurfaced, affecting many important political figures who were previously considered beyond suspicion. Today was the first meeting of the parliamentary Stavisky case review committee, and startling facts were discovered when they examined the documents related to the case. According to Stavisky's wife, Stavisky had lunch with former Minister of Commerce Durand in a large restaurant, but Durand still insists that he had no prior acquaintance with Stavisky. When Durand was in office, he advised insurance companies to purchase fake bonds from Bayonne in an official document. Furthermore, Stavisky's wife said that former Finance Minister Pierre-Étienne Flandin also dined with her husband at the Stresa Conference, but Flandin also denies ever seeing Stavisky. In addition, the owner of the L'Éclair newspaper, Dubarry, received a large amount of funding from Stavisky, and the newspaper has now been ordered to cease publication. However, Dubarry stated today during questioning by the parliamentary committee that the person who first introduced him to Stavisky was former Prime Minister Chautemps. Furthermore, the committee reviewed the number of checks issued by Stavisky during his lifetime, totaling as many as 800. Although only a portion has been collected, the names on them are already shocking. Apart from the 40 million francs that Stavisky spent himself, the banker Homer received as much as seven to eight million, and Stavisky's secretary Romaniello also received this amount. In addition, the amounts received by business tycoons, members of the Chamber of Deputies, and important political figures were also in the millions of francs, showing how lavishly Stavisky spent his money during his lifetime. (February 27th, Guomin News Agency dispatch)

(Paris) The parliamentary committee investigating the responsibility for the February 6th incident worked actively this afternoon. It was decided to obtain various documents on Thursday, examine them first, and then summon various witnesses for questioning next week, such as former Paris Police Chief Chiappe, former Prime Minister Chautemps, former Director of the Judicial Police Gischia, and former Director of the National Detective Squad Domegue. As a rule, civil servants are responsible for maintaining the confidentiality of matters within their duties. The government has now allowed the parliamentary investigation committee to allow civil servants who are summoned to testify before the committee not to maintain confidentiality. (February 27th, Havas News Agency dispatch)

(Paris) The Stavisky swindle case has been postponed for trial nineteen times. The committee responsible for investigating this matter has submitted a report, determining that the prosecutor of the Seine department, Pressard (the brother-in-law of former Prime Minister Chautemps), committed errors in his duties and should bear major responsibility. The Council of Ministers met at 9:00 PM tonight, and Minister of Justice Henry Chéron presented the report to the cabinet for review and asked President Lebrun to sign two orders, one to cancel the order appointing Pressard as a judge of the Supreme Court on February 3rd, and the other to appoint the public prosecutor of the Paris Court, Gommier, to replace Pressard as the prosecutor of the Seine department. As for Pressard, he will be appointed to another position. (February 27th, Havas News Agency dispatch)

Three Defendants in German Reichstag Fire Released

Naturalized as Russian Citizens

Arrived in Moscow and Were Welcomed

(Moscow) The defendants in the German Reichstag fire, Dimitrov, Popov, and Tanev, members of the Bulgarian Communist Party, were released from prison in Berlin and immediately flew to Russia. With the prior permission of the Russian authorities, they were naturalized as Russian citizens. When the three arrived at the airport here today, the crowd cheered, "Long live Dimitrov!" "Long live the Bulgarians!" They were then taken by cars prepared by the authorities to the Luxe Hotel, where rooms had already been reserved. A Reuters reporter visited them at the hotel, and Dimitrov, with a cigar in his mouth, said as he smoked and talked that although he had not suffered physical torture in prison, the mental and nervous pressure was sometimes worse than physical torture. The three Bulgarians were extremely happy and anticipated that demonstrations of joy would take place across the country after the news of their arrival was released. Lenin's wife and Lenin's sister presented Dimitrov with large bouquets of flowers. (February 28th, Reuters dispatch)

Shi Ying Goes from Hankou to Beijing

(Hankou) Shi Ying has repeatedly received telegrams from Wang Jingwei and Chiang Kai-shek urging him to resume his post. He boarded a ship for Beijing on the 28th, and his intention to resign may be rescinded. (February 28th)

Rumors of Restoration Abound, Austrian Political Situation Unstable

Archduke Otto's Activities in Belgium

France and Czechoslovakia Oppose Restoration of the Monarchy

Vienna: Over the past 36 hours, rumors have been rampant in Austria. Some say that a restoration of the monarchy is imminent, while others say that someone is plotting to assassinate Vice Chancellor Fey. The deadline for the ultimatum that the Austrian National Socialist Party supervisor Habicht issued to Austrian Chancellor Dr. Dollfuss in a previous radio address is due today, so the overall situation is particularly unstable, and fears of foreign interference are adding to the confusion caused by the rumors of restoration. It is reported that there have been secret messages exchanged recently between Vienna and a residence near Brussels (the residence of Archduke Otto, who claims to be the future monarch of Austria). A Reuters correspondent in Brussels has reported on this matter, saying that there has been unusual activity at the Archduke Otto's residence recently, but a formal statement issued by the residence stated that the Archduke does not wish to go to Austria.

According to a Reuters dispatch from Paris, a key figure said that the French government is now doing its utmost to oppose the restoration of the Habsburg monarchy. At the same time, political circles in Prague have denied the rumors that Czech troops are advancing towards the Austrian border, but have stated that the Czech government is now firmly opposed to the restoration of the monarchy in Austria. (February 28th, Reuters dispatch)

Austrian Home Guard Expresses Determination to Cooperate with the Government

Holds Determination to Maintain Austrian Independence

National Socialism Is Deeply Approved Of

But Unwilling to Have Internal Affairs Controlled by Others

Not Lightly Mentioning Restoration for Fear of Arousing Neighboring Countries' Displeasure

Vienna: Starhemberg strongly denied rumors of disagreements between the Home Guard and the Dollfuss government. It is claimed that we plan to implement our program in close cooperation with the Austrian Chancellor. We have no intention of using force or other plans that are disloyal to the country. We are now determined to cooperate with Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss with complete loyalty. We have absolute faith in him. All rumors are being intentionally spread by someone. (February 28th, Reuters dispatch)

Vienna: Starhemberg said today in response to questions from media representatives that the Home Guard advocates the immediate repeal of laws excluding members of the Habsburg monarchy from residing in Austria, but the question of restoration cannot be answered hastily at this time. That question is not purely an Austrian matter but also involves the future of neighboring countries, so Austria cannot rashly raise it. As for electing a regent, it is difficult to implement because there are no such provisions in Austrian law. The Home Guard is well aware that Austrian communist elements have sufficient weapons, so violent conflict may ultimately be unavoidable. However, now that obvious obstacles have been removed, the pressing task is to be loyal to the suffering people. Starhemberg also mentioned National Socialism, saying that the Home Guard strongly approves of German National Socialism and Pan-Germanism, but the best way to implement this ideology is to maintain Austrian independence. We welcome the restoration of friendly relations with Germany, but we are unwilling to have Austrian internal affairs controlled by National Socialism. (February 27th, Guomin News Agency dispatch)

Ultimatum Requiring Cooperation with Germany Expires

Authorities Prepare Everything to Cope with Events

Vienna: The Austrian National Socialist Party inspector Habicht previously announced to the Austrians by radio, urging them to cooperate with Germany, otherwise, one

A week later, he will resume his activities against the Austrian government. This statement is like an ultimatum, and the deadline expired this afternoon. Austria is quite worried because Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss has firmly rejected his request for cooperation. There have not been any incidents yet, but the police have prepared everything. (February 28th, Reuters dispatch)

8,000 Italian Troops Stationed on Austrian Border

Vienna: It is now known that during the recent Austrian Socialist Party rebellion, 8,000 Italian troops were stationed in Padua, ready to rush to the Austrian border in an emergency. It is reported that although the authorities have not decided what necessary measures to take, the troops are fully prepared to deal with any incidents. (February 28th, Reuters dispatch)

Border Conflict Rumors Denied

Rumors of incidents occurring on the Austro-German border have been denied by Austrian Chancellor Dollfuss to a Reuters reporter in Vienna, who stated that everything in Austria is peaceful and that they are now on guard to prevent incidents from occurring on the border. He also stated that the Austrian government has not sent troops to the Czech border but has only ordered several auxiliary troops to Upper Austria to maintain public order there. (Reuters)

Italy, Austria, and Hungary Form Economic Alliance

With the Approval of France

Austrian Authorities Issue Announcement

Vienna: Rumors have spread that France will take action regarding the economic alliance agreed upon by Italy, Austria, and Hungary, and that Austrian troops and the Home Guard are being transferred to the Austro-German border to prevent unexpected incidents after February 28th. The Government Information Office has now issued an announcement denying these rumors. It is said that the discussions between Austria and Hungary did not involve the issue of a customs union but only sought to establish close economic cooperation between the three countries in accordance with the resolutions agreed upon at the Stresemann Conference in October 1932 and approved by France, and to conclude an agreement on the allocation of preferential tariffs. (February 28th, Guomin News Agency dispatch)

Austrian and Hungarian Prime Ministers to Meet in Rome

Austrian Chancellor Dr. Dollfuss and Hungarian Prime Minister Gömbös are now scheduled to go to Rome around March 12th for three days to discuss plans for the economic resolution of the Danube countries with Italian Premier Mussolini. The plan stipulates that the three countries will mutually grant tariff concessions and open up a sea route for Austria and Hungary through Trieste and Fiume. This can be seen as proof that Italy is changing its attitude towards Germany. According to a Reuters dispatch from Rome, Italian political circles deny that Italy, Austria, and Hungary have a plan to form a formal political group along the lines of the Little Entente, which is formed by the three countries of Czechoslovakia, Romania, and Yugoslavia. Italian political circles also firmly stated that the cooperation between Italy, Austria, and Hungary emphasizes economics, that the plan is not aimed at antagonizing any country, and that it can benefit Germany and the Little Entente countries. (Reuters)

Budapest: According to "Magyar Hirlap", former Hungarian Prime Minister Count Bethlen will go to Rome in the first week of March. It was originally scheduled for the Austrian and Hungarian prime ministers to meet with Italian Premier Mussolini in Rome in March. Bethlen's visit to Italy today is before the meeting of the three prime ministers of Italy, Austria, and Hungary, but it is said that Bethlen's visit to Mussolini is of a private nature. (February 28th, Havas dispatch)

Tyrol Provincial Assembly Dissolved

At the same time, the Tyrol province in western Austria has taken organized professional national action. The provincial assembly has dissolved itself and handed over its duties to the governor, who will add three representatives of the Home Guard to the provincial government and organize a so-called advisory committee of twelve representatives from the industrial, commercial, and religious sectors. The committee plans to serve temporarily until the local councils are reorganized according to the "Guild" system, which is what the Home Guard demands. (February 28th, Reuters dispatch)

French Newspapers Disbelieve Austrian Restoration

(Paris) The diplomatic circles here are quite doubtful about the news of the restoration of the Habsburg royal family in Austria, considering it mere newspaper rumors and not credible. Therefore, they are unwilling to comment on it. However, they state that the restoration would not only cause political difficulties but also contradict the promises made by the Austrian and Hungarian governments to the great powers. On February 4, 1920, and April 1, 1921, the Conference of Ambassadors of various countries sent notes to the Austrian and Hungarian governments twice, stating that the restoration of the Habsburg royal family would be regarded as fundamentally contrary to the peace treaty. The allied countries would not only fail to recognize it but also be unable to tolerate it. At that time, Austria and Hungary replied acknowledging their compliance with the warnings from various countries. As for Hungary, after the failure of King Charles' restoration attempt, it also agreed not to attempt such a thing again, and its promise was even more formal. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Established under the orders of a certain neighboring country

People from all walks of life were involved

Budapest A large-scale espionage case has recently been uncovered here, with the agency spread throughout the country. The police have not announced the number of people arrested in this case, but it must be quite a few. According to a government announcement, people from all walks of life were involved in the case. This spy agency specialized in gathering information about military strength and military training methods. According to private sources, this agency was established under the orders of a certain neighboring country. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

US Congress Refuses to Meet with Hunger Marchers

Labor Party's Motion Ultimately Rejected

(London) The House of Commons tonight rejected a motion to extend the session to draw the attention of Members of Parliament to the Prime Minister's refusal to meet with representatives of the unemployed. The motion was proposed by Buchanan, a left-wing leader of the Labor Party, and seconded by Labor opposition leader Samuel and others from the Independent Liberal Party. They were met with jeers when seconding the motion. The motion was ultimately rejected by 270 votes to 52. In response to questioning, Prime Minister MacDonald stated that previous governments and the Trades Union Congress had refused to meet with representatives of the unemployed. He believed that meeting with representatives of the unemployed, whether privately or in Parliament, would not benefit the unemployed. No government or prime minister would allow such politically motivated behavior. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

US Establishes New Bank to Develop Foreign Trade

Extends Huge Loan to Cuba

For the purpose of purchasing silver

(Washington) The United States will establish two specialized banks to develop trade relations with China and Soviet Russia. In addition to this, it is possible that banks will be established in South America and Europe. However, due to political relations, a special bank will be established to manage trade with Cuba, separate from the banks managing trade with other countries. The bank established for Cuban trade will have a capital of 11 million yuan, and its business will be to replace the China Consortium in making loans. According to those in charge, after this bank is established, it will lend several million yuan to the Cuban government. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(Washington) It is expected here that the US government will lend several million yuan to the Cuban government to purchase silver in the US. The exact amount is still unknown, but it is generally believed that this silver will be minted into Cuban currency. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

(New York) It is still unknown how much silver Cuba will purchase from the US, but well-informed sources say 20 million yuan. According to the New York Times, this plan could dispel the opposition of Cuban sugar producers to the Cuban sugar quota. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

(Washington) In addition to serving as the chairman of the newly established Export-Import Bank, Peek also serves as a foreign trade consultant, thus wielding almost dictatorial power in foreign trade. Peek stated last night that agriculture must restore its proper place in national life, which shows that the authorities intend to emphasize agriculture and de-emphasize industry. This matter involves many tariff revisions. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

US Launches Blue Eagle Movement, Plans Extensive Program

To Revise and Organize Industrial and Commercial Regulations

To Stabilize Prices and Suppress Under-Selling

Johnson Convenes Meeting of Industrialists

So that they may freely express their criticisms

(Washington) General Johnson, Director of the Economic Recovery Administration, declared to a majority of industrialists today that an extensive plan has been formulated to revise and organize the various regulations of American industry and commerce. In addition, he plans to organize public meetings so that all interested parties can express their opinions. Before any criticism from various parties, Johnson explained in advance that he firmly believes that the economic recovery plan is making progress, and said that he has formulated an extensive plan to correct any imperfections in the recovery measures. The main points of his plan are roughly as follows: (1) Establish more uniform and fair rules to stabilize prices and use more effective methods of suppressing price drops below cost. (2) Unify wage rates and working hours for competing industries, and divide the country into several regions according to wage levels, so as to reduce working hours and increase wages. (3) Protect small businesses from the oppression of monopolies. (4) Establish new methods to make the various sectors more receptive to various regulations. (5) Stipulate the conditions for the allocation of funds for the Regulations Affairs Bureau (i.e., the Recovery Bureau) so as not to be influenced by oppression and other forces. (6) Delete conflicting provisions in various regulations to make them perfect. (7) Set up representatives of labor and consumers on the councils of the Regulations Affairs Bureau (i.e., the Recovery Bureau), with government representatives participating. (8) Solve various methods used in labor-capital conflicts and make good use of them. General Johnson concluded that organizing meetings to allow all parties to express their opinions is a sincere effort to remedy the shortcomings of the various regulations. In addition, Johnson also declared to more than 4,000 people that if necessary, various regulations can be amended by order of the President. After the amendments, if industrialists make requests, they can still be corrected. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Canada Ratifies Silver Agreement, New York Silver Market Rebounds

(New York) The securities market today was relatively quiet. Although there was slight improvement in the bearish news during today's trading, it is generally expected that there will be no major changes in the short term, as there is still no concrete news about the Securities Market Control Act. Therefore, the best approach at present seems to be to remain neutral.

The silver market opened weaker today, then rebounded slightly, and finally was firmer. This was probably the result of Canada ratifying the London Silver Agreement.

The cotton market position is actually more stable than before. Some experts advise people to buy when prices fall. Buying interest was strong at the opening, and the market was firm, but later selling pressure was stronger.

Rubber prices tended to weaken today, as other markets in the US were generally uncertain, and there was no concrete news about the rubber restriction plan. Therefore, although overseas news was not bad, it could not revive the morale here. Several parties advise operators to continue to realize profits until there is definite news about the restriction measures. Wheat prices initially fell and then rose today. The reasons for the rebound were: first, the firmness of the Winnipeg wheat market; second, the over-selling of positions. Since this actual position is already more stable than before, there is a saying in the wheat market that it is quite safe to buy now. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Change of British Troops in Pingjin

(Tianjin) The British troops stationed in Pingjin are being rotated. Eighty British soldiers stationed in Ping arrived in Tianjin on the afternoon of the 28th, and the Japanese soldiers stationed in Tianjin will leave for Ping on the 5th. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

Prelude to a Farce in Changchun

｜Puyi is Preparing to Don Robes and Mount the Throne｜

(Changchun) The various preparations for Puyi's usurpation have been completed here. The officials of the "Manchukuo" executive government have completed various plans, and the court robes have also been made. The palace is setting up the objects to be used during the court session, so that they can be used after March 1st. According to the old customs of the late Qing Dynasty, the emperor was not easily seen when he ascended the throne. Therefore, only a small number of Japanese and "Manchu" people and Mongolians can participate in the usurpation ceremony. The newly built Temple of Heaven has four layers and three stone steps. The jade seal of the puppet emperor has already been made. The first ceremony will be held in the Temple of Heaven, and the second will be held in Puyi's palace. It has not yet been decided what kind of ceremonial dress Puyi will wear when he usurps the throne, but an upper general's ceremonial dress and a court dress embroidered with golden dragons have been made. Puyi will wear the uniform at the Temple of Heaven. There is now a new 1934 model car for Puyi's use, but it does not carry a crown, only a French monk's gauze cap embroidered with the "Manchukuo" flag and decorated with gemstones. This cap was custom-made in Japan. At present, the population of Changchun has suddenly increased. The people have no particularly enthusiastic expression, but it is feared that more people will come here before Thursday. Some Japanese have already arrived here, and Mongolians with strange costumes are often seen on the streets. Foreign reporters, film and sound film experts have come here to prepare to take news. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Central Political Council Passes Principles for Mongolian Autonomy

Mongolian Representatives Decide to Accept

Sends Qin Zhen to Europe and the United States to Study Justice

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council held its 397th meeting on the morning of the 28th, attended by more than 30 people including Wang Zhaoming, Ye Chucang, Ju Zheng, Sun Ke, Kong Xiangxi, and Shao Yuanchong, with Sun Ke presiding.

(1) Approved eight principles for the Mongolian autonomy issue:

(1) A Mongolian Local Autonomy Administration Affairs Committee shall be established in a suitable location in Mongolia, subordinate to the Executive Yuan and under the guidance of the central competent authority, to manage the political affairs of each league and banner. The chairman and members shall be Mongolian personnel in principle, and the expenses shall be paid by the central government. The central government shall also send senior officials to be stationed at the location of the committee to guide it and to mediate disputes between leagues, banners, provinces, and counties in the vicinity. (2) The league offices shall be renamed league governments, and the banner offices shall be renamed banner governments, with no change in their organization. The expenses of the banner governments shall be subsidized by the central government. (3) The Chahar Department shall be renamed banner to show uniformity, and its system and organization shall remain the same. (4) The jurisdiction of each league and banner shall remain the same. (5) The existing pastures of each league and banner shall be closed to reclamation, and the economy of the area shall be developed through the improvement of animal husbandry and the establishment of related industries. (However, those leagues and banners that voluntarily cultivate shall be allowed to do so.) (6) The original taxes of the leagues and banners and the private rents of the Mongolian people shall be protected. (7) The local taxes collected by provinces and counties in the leagues and banners shall be allocated to the leagues and banners in certain amounts as construction funds. The method of tax allocation shall be determined separately. (8) No new counties or bureaus shall be established in the league and banner areas in the future. (However, when it is necessary to establish them, the consent of the related leagues and banners must be obtained.) (2) Resolved to send Qin Zhen to Europe and the United States to study justice.

(3) Approved a budget estimate. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Nanjing) The representatives of Inner Mongolia met at 2:00 p.m. on the 28th to discuss the eight principles of the Inner Mongolia Autonomy Measures passed by the Central Political Council. They all agreed that they were in line with the actual situation and decided to accept them unanimously and report to each league and banner. President Wang is scheduled to summon the representatives for talks at 3:00 p.m. on the 1st. According to the representatives, the previous plan had some points that could be discussed, so they asked for a review in Beijing. Fortunately, Wang, Jiang, Dai, and other authorities made revisions and submitted them to the Central Political Council. This morning's passage is in line with the Inner Mongolian situation, and we have decided to accept it and are very grateful to the central government for its concern for Inner Mongolian autonomy. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Nanjing) The Mongolian representatives considered that the eight principles for solving the Mongolian autonomy issue passed by the Central Political Council on the 28th were suitable for the Mongolian situation. Therefore, in the afternoon, they convened a meeting of representatives in Beijing and resident representatives to decide that the representatives should report to the princes of each league and banner and send a telegram to thank the central government for its good intentions. They will also issue a written telegram to the whole country in the name of the representatives in Beijing to express their acceptance. According to a certain representative, they plan to visit President Wang on the 1st to thank him for handling the Mongolian affairs. They also intend to state their opinions on the organization and location of the Mongolian Local Autonomy Political Affairs Committee and the organization methods of the league and banner governments for reference. Although the central government has determined the principles on the issue of Mongolian banner taxation, the specific distribution method still needs to wait for them to report to the princes of each league and banner in Mongolia and the authorities of the Chahar and Suiyuan provinces to consult in detail, formulate opinions, and then send a telegram to the central government for review before a decision can be made. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

Draft Constitution Announced

President and Vice President to Serve Six-Year Terms

(Nanjing) The draft constitution is scheduled to be announced on the 1st. Its content stipulates that the President and Vice President shall serve six-year terms and may be re-elected for one consecutive term. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

The staff will be paid their February salaries and dismissed, and the Yuan will introduce them to work as appropriate. All seals and documents have been transferred to the Secretariat. Unfinished matters will be handled by the Deliberation Section. Documents criticizing the draft constitution from various places will be collected by the Compilation and Review Office. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

Song Ziwen to Inspect Northwest

Departure in Three Weeks

Dai Chuanxian also plans to go

(Nanjing) Song Ziwen met with reporters at Shenshi on the 28th and said that the development of the Northwest is extremely important, so he decided to go and inspect it in person. The departure is scheduled in about three weeks. He will take the Jinpu Railway and then the Longhai Railway. The director of the Xi'an Office, Liu Wenshan, and a group of 17 people have already set off and will arrive soon. In the future, he will also go to Lanzhou, Qinghai, and Ningxia, and then transfer to Sichuan. He is afraid that he will not be able to go to Xinjiang due to time constraints. The date of his return to Beijing will depend on the situation. The scope of the inspection will include the conditions of roads, water conservancy, bridges, agriculture, forestry, industry, commerce, animal husbandry, and social economy and culture. In addition to rectifying the Northwest health cause, the Central Committee also plans to establish a veterinary institute. President Dai has always paid close attention to the situation in the Northwest, and it is gratifying that he can go with him. As for the silver issue, it is handled by the Ministry of Finance, and no opinions have been expressed. Song Kaiyun agreed to a certain newspaper company's request to accompany him to the Northwest. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

(Nanjing) Presidents Wang and Dai visited Song Ziwen at noon on the 28th and discussed for a long time. Song will return to Shanghai within a few days to prepare his luggage and will accompany Dai to inspect the Northwest next month. According to a Central News Agency reporter, they will first go north to Xi'an, then to Lanzhou, cross the Han River from Lan, and then enter Sichuan by plane. The trip to Xinjiang was cancelled. The Northwest is our lifeline. In recent years, natural disasters and man-made disasters have caused the people to suffer extremely. We should actively develop it. A Northwest Office has now been established in Xi'an. I plan to personally promote the development of roads and water conservancy there. The important roads are: one is the section from Xi'an to Lanzhou, extending to Xinjiang, and the other is the section from Xi'an to Sichuan, which is also planned. The loans for cotton and wheat are calculated in gold coins. The increase in the price of silver has no impact. The rumor that there are losses is not accurate. However, the output of national cotton this year and the difficulty in selling cotton are being negotiated to reduce orders and modify contracts. I am the person involved in the White Silver Agreement, so it is inconvenient to express my opinion. I also did not attend today's Central Political Council meeting. I am also unable to express my opinion on the countermeasures for the US raising the price of silver because I am not in charge. (Central News Agency dispatch, 18th)

Ministry of Industry and Commerce Prepares to Restore Farmers Bank

(Nanjing) In order to restore the Farmers Bank, which was sponsored by the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce of the former Beijing government, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce sent Mei Zheyuan to Shanghai to contact the banking industry to discuss investment and restoration methods. Executive Yuan Orders City and County Governments to be Cautious Regarding Justice

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan ordered the judicial organs in each city and county government, saying that each level of government often arrests and detains people who appeal, sometimes for months or years, which is a neglect of the law. County governments that also handle judicial affairs have also failed to comply with Article 73 of the Criminal Procedure Law, trampling on human rights and violating the spirit of a country ruled by law. In the future, each provincial and municipal government shall not engage in the above-mentioned illegal acts. If it is found that detained prisoners have not yet been sent, they must be transferred to the judicial organs for review within 24 hours of receiving the document. County governments that also handle judicial affairs are also ordered to comply with Article 73 of the Criminal Procedure Law in order to promote the rule of law and respect human rights. (Special Dispatch, 28th)
