Zhang Kaiyun, Secretary of the Tianjin Municipal Party Department, Assassinated

(Tianjin) Zhang Kaiyun, secretary of the Propaganda Section of the Tianjin Municipal Party Department, was shot and killed by three young men at 4:00 a.m. this morning in his residence at the Fozhao Building on No. 4 Road in the French Concession. He suffered seven injuries and died on the spot. Before committing the murder, the three young men held work permits and asked to see him. The tea servant led them into Zhang's room. Zhang was still asleep when he was shot. The Municipal Party Department is doing its best to investigate the cause. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Zhang Kaiyun, the secretary of the Tianjin Municipal Party Department who was killed in Fozhao Building this morning, was in his forties and from Hunan. He handled special affairs for the Party Department and had lived in Fozhao Building for two years. He used to live at No. 37 in the back building. On the 25th, he and two friends opened room 28 of the hotel. One of the two friends left and one stayed. The person who stayed was named Zhang Baojian, and the hotel book registered him as a Shangdong person, 30 years old, a merchant of Fushengguan. He went out that night and did not return. On the night of the 27th, he returned to the residence with him. At 4:00 a.m. on the 28th, he sneaked into Zhang Kaiyun's room and shot him to death. The court examined the body in the afternoon, and the Party Department will prepare a coffin for burial one day. (Special Dispatch, 28th)

Yunnanese People's Stance on the British Troops' Occupation of Banhong

The People's Diplomacy Support Association Issues a Declaration

Announcing the Process of the Banhong Boundary Demarcation Negotiations

Kunming Correspondence: After British troops invaded the Yunnan border from Burma a few days ago, the situation became extremely tense. Recently, the Yunnan People's Diplomacy Support Association issued a declaration on this case. The original text is as follows:

"Our country is unfortunate, with disasters occurring one after another, internal strife following internal strife, and foreign insults increasing day by day. Since the 'September 18th Incident,' the Northeast has fallen, the national strength is insufficient, and the lost territories have not been recovered, which is heartbreaking. Our province borders strong neighbors, and the dangerous situation is no less than that of the Northeast. People with insight are all worried and angry. Therefore, they organized a national salvation association, raised national salvation funds, and strived to build border defenses to secure our territory and prevent covetousness. This is also the only way for the Yunnanese people to save the country. However, just as things were being planned, alarming news came. The British imperialists, disregarding justice and treaties, taking advantage of our country being preoccupied with many affairs and unable to attend to the border areas, repeated the old trick of forcibly occupying Pianma, sent troops to occupy our Banhong, and are forcing us into this situation. How can we sit idly by? For the sake of preserving territory and safeguarding national rights, the Yunnanese people must rise up in unison and vow to fight the imperialists to fulfill the patriotic duty of the people. Therefore, we have united various groups to form the Yunnan People's Diplomacy Support Association, pooling our wisdom and strength to serve as a backing for the government.

It is verified that Banhong is our territory and rich in various metal minerals, which the British have coveted for a long time. The reason why they have hesitated in the past is simply because the Hulu King's inclination towards us was strong and he could not be bribed. Recently, with their cunning revealed, they have not hesitated to blatantly rely on force to carry out aggression. (A brief outline of Banhong is attached below to clarify the truth.) Although Banhong is only a small corner of land, it is of great importance to our country's territorial sovereignty. The only way to deal with it is to earnestly request the government to lodge a strong protest, argue on the basis of reason, and demand that the British troops withdraw first, and stop all activities of British and Burmese people in the area, to avoid accidents and major disputes. The permanent fundamental solution is to earnestly request the government to demarcate the boundary with the British as soon as possible. If the boundary can be demarcated, all the outstanding issues of the Tuojiao issue, the Pianma issue, the Banhong issue, the Yichun issue, the Sichun issue, and the determined and undetermined boundaries can be resolved comprehensively. Otherwise, the British's insidious encroachment will be no less than the Japanese's violent annexation. Having obtained Tuojiao, they will then occupy Pianma; having obtained Pianma, they will then occupy Banhong. If they obtain Banhong, they will then occupy the western counties of Yunnan. In less than ten years, our Yunnan may become a continuation of the Northeast. Thinking of this, we cannot help but shudder. Therefore, the Yunnanese people should recognize that demarcating the boundary is the only way to resolve disputes and prevent aggression, and strive to achieve it. We also hope that the people of the whole country will rise up to help, and that the Yunnan Provincial Government and the Central Government will work together to negotiate earnestly, and will not stop until the goal of demarcating the boundary is achieved. This is the primary meaning of the purpose of this Association.

Although Banhong is our country's territory, it is far from the provincial capital and has long been regarded as a wilderness. Moreover, due to frequent troubles in recent years, we have not been able to pay attention to management. Therefore, the situation in the area is mostly vague, and we are often misled in negotiations. If we want to negotiate and demarcate with the British, it will be futile if we do not first conduct an investigation. Otherwise, if we do not know the enemy and ourselves, we will have no basis for negotiations, and even if justice is upheld and things are returned to their rightful owners, there may be no way to develop and construct it. Therefore, the Yunnanese people should quickly organize an inspection team to conduct on-site investigations, which can help diplomacy and lay the foundation for future construction, which is the best of both worlds. This is the secondary meaning of the purpose of this Association.

For these two meanings, we hope that the Yunnanese people will be down-to-earth, work hard, continue to work hard, persevere, not be intimidated by the British's power and harbor fear, not be motivated by temporary anger and overstep the bounds, not forget things after they are over and leave a bad name for five-minute enthusiasm, and not treat each other as strangers, lest we suffer the dissipation of a pile of loose sand. Then, our territory can be preserved, and our national rights can be asserted. Gu Tinglin said, 'The rise and fall of the world is the responsibility of every individual.' Mencius said, 'A country must first be attacked by itself before others attack it.' What to do is up to us to choose and encourage ourselves. This declaration is hereby made in the hope of public scrutiny."

Attached: Brief Outline of Banhong

(A) Location of Banhong: Banhong is under the jurisdiction of the Upper Hulu King, commonly known as the Savage Mountains, located in the southwest corner of this province, bordering Shuangjiang County to the east, Burma to the west, the Gengma and Mengding indigenous officials of Shunning and Zhenkang counties to the north, and the Menglian indigenous official under Lancang County to the south. The area is rich in various metal minerals, and gemstones and jade are found everywhere. The people are collectively referred to as "savages."

(B) History of the Banhong Boundary Demarcation: In the winter of the 25th year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty (1899 AD), our side sent Liu Wansheng, the garrison of Tengyue, and Chen Can, the circuit intendant of western Yunnan, to demarcate the boundary together with the British official Skerd according to the original map agreed upon by Xue Fucheng, the envoy to Britain, and the British Foreign Office. At the meeting in Huban, it was agreed according to the yellow line on Xue's map that the areas belonging to Banhong would belong to us, and the areas belonging to Banguang would belong to Burma. During the demarcation, Skerd suddenly said that the longitude and latitude of Xue's map did not match the text of the treaty, and presented another small map, requesting that the boundary be determined according to the red line on the map. As a result, all the areas of Banhong and the lands of the indigenous officials of Mengjiao and Mengzhe were all designated as belonging to Burma. Liu Zhen and Chen Dao insisted that the British official had changed the line and encroached on the land, and agreed to each draw a line and request instructions from their respective governments. Subsequently, in the lines proposed for concession by both sides and the line reviewed and instructed by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, although the lands of the two indigenous officials of Mengjiao and Menglian were still designated as belonging to British Burma, the areas of Banhong remained completely belonging to us. This is a rough outline of the demarcation situation on that day.

(C) Current Situation of Banhong: It was recently reported that on December 14th of the twenty-second year, seven or eight British people suddenly arrived in Banhong, summoned the local people, and held a secret meeting. On the 19th, it was discovered that there were about 2,000 British soldiers, each carrying equipment and tools. Wherever they went, they immediately built roads for automobiles and repaired iron bridges on the Banhong River. It was also reported that Ma, a Hui Muslim from Bannong, was a descendant of those who fled from Yongchang after Du Wenxiu's defeat. He had considerable influence in the area and had been contacted and drugged by the British, willingly serving as a dog for the British. He secretly offered the map of the Banhong factory and used small favors to win over the Hulu King. The Hulu King refused, so the British used force to oppress and carry out aggression. This is a general overview of the recent situation in Banhong.

The Western Route Army Encircles the Xiao and Gao Bandit Gangs

He Jian Encourages the Soldiers

To Complete the Entire Mission

Changsha Correspondence: After the First Column of the Western Route Army broke through Xiao Ke's old nest, Yongxin, and the Second Column recaptured Kong Hechong's old nest, Xiaoyuan, the bandits lost all their support and fled in panic. Except for Kong Hechong, who is hiding in the deep mountains of Lianhua and Yongxin in western Jiangxi and has no ability to move for the time being, the two bandits Xiao Ke and Gao Yongsheng (Gao was the commander of the pseudo-16th Division under Kong Hechong) fled from Wanzai, Yifeng, Gaoan, Xiushui, and Wuning to the area between Ruichang and Wuning on the border of Hubei and Jiangxi, running hundreds of li in two weeks. Before they could catch their breath, Liu Yinggu, Commander of the Second Column of the Western Route Army, immediately led Peng Weiren's division of the First Column, Zhu Yaohua and Yue Sen's two divisions of the Second Column, and Zhong Guangren's brigade, together with Guo Rudong's division and Li Zongjian and Liu Peixu's two independent brigades of the Third Column, into long-pursuit teams and interception teams, using a large encirclement to strive to encircle and annihilate them. The deployment is as follows: (1) Liu Yinggu himself is stationed in Wuning, commanding the three divisions of Peng, Zhu, and Yue, and Zhong Guangren's brigade, to pursue closely, so that the bandits have no time to flee. (2) Guo Rudong and the two brigades of Liu and Li are assembled on the border of Ruichang, Wuning, and southern Hubei to intercept, so that the bandits cannot flee into southern Hubei. At the same time, Chairman Chiang was telegraphed to deploy the Northern Route Army to coordinate the interception in the De'an area. It seems that with the Yangtze River in front, pursuing troops behind, and heavy troops guarding dangerous passes on both sides, the bandit gang of more than 10,000 people is now trapped in a heavy encirclement, gathering in the Yangduan, Xiaoao, and Henggang areas between Ruichang and Wuning, becoming fish in a kettle. Liu Yinggu is currently actively deploying troops, pressing forward step by step, and expects to drive the bandits into a corner and launch a general attack from all sides to annihilate them. Therefore, there will be a fierce battle in the Yangduan and Henggang areas in the coming days. He Jian, Commander-in-Chief of the Western Route Army, anticipates that the two bandits Xiao and Gao will definitely be annihilated this time, and yesterday issued an order to encourage the commanders of the First, Second, and Third Columns, Liu Jianxu, Liu Yinggu, and Chen Jicheng, and the Jiangfang Commander Li Yunjie along the Gan River, as well as the army and division commanders of the Western Route Army, to make further efforts to complete the entire mission. The telegram provided very detailed instructions on the direction that the various units should strive for in the future. The original order stated, "It has been found that since our army has been pursuing and suppressing bandits in western Jiangxi and southern Hubei, it has achieved repeated successes, fought fiercely with the bandit gangs many times, and recovered many bandit areas. The old nests of Xiaoyuan, Meihua, and Yongxin have also been successively recovered. The bandits' base has been completely lost. Although their main force has not yet been annihilated, they have already become fish in a kettle and are expected to have difficulty surviving. Moreover, the two gangs of Xiao and Gao have become increasingly desperate after being repeatedly oppressed by our army and are having difficulty catching their breath. Although they are currently entrenched in the mountainous areas on the border of Ruichang and Wuning, attempting to survive, the combined forces of our army have been formed, and the units pursuing and suppressing them are all particularly diligent. It will not be difficult to capture them in one fell swoop. What the commander-in-chief hopes from the various units in the future is: (1) The Second and Third Columns should maintain close contact and strive to press the two bandits Xiao and Gao to the northeast in a large encirclement, coordinating with the Nanchang-Jiujiang Railway troops to annihilate them in the Ruichang-Wuning border area or drive them into the Yangtze River to be submerged. (2) The First Column's troops in the eastern border of Lianhua and Chaling should quickly advance eastward and maintain contact with the Yongxin troops to eliminate the remaining bandits in the Yongxin-Lianhua-Mi (Gang) area. If necessary, the Anfu and Taianli troops should also advance southwestward as soon as possible to restore the normal state of the counties in southwestern Jiangxi. (3) The troops along the Gan River in western Jiangxi should strive to build more blockhouses and fortifications to create an iron wall on the west bank of the Gan River, so that the bandits in eastern Jiangxi have no possibility of fleeing west. This matter has been repeatedly ordered to be strictly complied with, but it has not been effectively done. Efforts must be intensified in the future, and the existing fortifications should not be considered sufficient. (4) Division Commander Tao (Guang) should comply with the new order and quickly complete the fortifications and blockhouses on both sides of the Yuan River, so that the bandits in southwestern Jiangxi and northeastern Jiangxi cannot communicate. (5) The troops currently stationed in southern Hubei should quickly eliminate the remaining bandits, and the troops repairing the riverbank should rush to construct continuous fortifications and strive to prevent the bandits in the areas to the north from crossing south. (6) The units clearing and suppressing Xiaoyuan and the western parts of Wanzai and Yifeng should make special efforts to clear and suppress and report as soon as possible that they have been cleared. The above are the duties of the commanders of the various units and are also a good opportunity to complete the entire mission of our army. It is hoped that everyone will understand this intention, muster the last of their courage, and achieve the glorious reputation of saving the country and the nation. There are high hopes for this." (February 25th)

A Male Floating Corpse Found in the Northern Suburbs of Songjiang

A male corpse was suddenly found yesterday in Shiwutu, outside the North Gate of the city. The corpse was about thirty years old and wearing a dark blue cotton-padded jacket and trousers. The Shiwutu township police reported to the Procuratorate, which dispatched an official to the countryside today for an examination. The examination revealed no injuries to the body, and it appeared to be a suicide by drowning. A coroner's report was filled out and submitted, and the Procuratorate will issue a notice to claim the body. The township police have been instructed to provide a coffin for burial.

A Rural Woman Run Over and Killed by a Bus on the Suzhou-Jiaxing Road in Suzhou

At 10:00 AM on the morning of the day before yesterday, a long-distance bus on the Suzhou-Jiaxing Road, the third direct Suzhou-Jiaxing bus departing from Suzhou, Suzhou No. 3, with Tang Qisheng as the driver and Guan A'gen as the co-driver, was driving near Bridge No. 46, about three kilometers away from Shengze, at 12:16 PM, when they suddenly saw a rural woman 400 meters ahead, slowly walking and blocking the road. They immediately honked the horn to warn her, but the woman was deaf and continued to walk slowly as before. In an instant, the bus was close to her, and the driver urgently steered to the left to avoid her, but because there was a small river on the left, it was impossible to avoid her. The woman was knocked down by the rear fender, and her head was crushed by the wheels and she died. After the incident occurred, Wang Bi, the director of the Shengze Public Security Bureau, and the supervising inspector of Wujiang County rushed to investigate the truth and reported it to the county government. Magistrate Wang went to the countryside yesterday (the 28th) to investigate. It is reported that the deceased was named Shen Bao, 48 years old, from Qizizhen. Her husband's name is Shen Baguan. Shen Bao was returning home from a relative's gathering that day and unexpectedly met with this disaster. The driver who caused the accident returned to Suzhou that day to report the details of the accident to the Suzhou General Bureau. It is said that the accident was not the driver's fault, but was caused by the deceased's deafness, her failure to avoid the bus, and her panic after seeing the bus, resulting in this tragic accident of a person being killed by a bus on the Suzhou-Jiaxing Road for the first time since it opened.

A Strange Tale of a Birth of Five Monkeys

A woman named Pu, a villager in the Li family area, four li west of Chefang outside the Fengmen Gate, 39 years old this year, suddenly gave birth to five monkeys at 10:00 PM on the night before last (the 27th). Mother and children are still safe, and the neighbors all think it is a strange event. The number of people going to see them is overwhelming.

Establishment of the Wuxi Construction Bureau

The Construction Bureau of this county was merged into the county government at the end of February last year, and a technical office was established separately to comprehensively manage construction matters. Zhang Dezai, a native of the county, was appointed as the technical director to handle all affairs. It has been more than a year since then. Recently, the Jiangsu Provincial Government considered local construction to be important, and it was decided through a provincial government meeting to restore the construction bureaus of six counties, including Wuxi. Director Zhang was still appointed to take charge of the Construction Bureau of this county. The county was informed and the letter of appointment and seal were issued. Preparations are now complete, and the bureau is still attached to the county government. It is scheduled to be formally established today. On the one hand, Director Zhang is re-compiling the budget and submitting it to the county for verification.

Implementation of New Measuring Instruments in the Rice Industry

Since receiving the order to promote weights and measures, the county government of this county has been actively carrying out the work. Weighing instruments have been replaced with the new system in accordance with the order, but measuring instruments have not been implemented. This is because it is difficult to implement the new system for measuring instruments used in the rice and bean industry. After the Rice and Bean Industry Association persuaded various rice shops and warehouses to adopt the new system, a meeting was held to discuss the intention of promotion and explain it in detail. It was agreed that starting from April 1st of this year, new instruments would be prepared. Once ready, the county government would be requested to send inspectors to the meeting for verification. It was decided that the new system would be uniformly adopted from May 1st to standardize the measurements.

Active Development of Long-Distance Telephone by the Construction Department

The development of long-distance telephone in Jiangsu Province is far behind that of Zhejiang Province. Only the following twelve counties have exchanges that are slightly formed and can communicate with each other: Nanjing, Lishui, Jurong (including the rural lines of Tianwang Temple and Chenwuzhuang), Zhenjiang (including the rural lines of Sibaitou, Gaozi, and Tanzhu), Danyang (including the rural lines of Lucheng and Erling), Jintan, Liyang, Wujin (including the rural lines of Banzha and Benniu), Yixing (including the rural lines of Shushan Dingshan, Xushe, and Zhangzhu), Jiangyin, Changshu, Wuxi, Wuxian, and Wujiang. In Wuxi, the following nine rural lines have been registered: Dangkou, Zhangjingqiao, Donghutang, Chenshu, Yangjian, Xueyanqiao, Yanjiaqiao, Hudai, and Zhaimen. At the same time, they can connect to the urban telephone for conversation. After the new machines are replaced, the connection will be more responsive, and words can be used to represent speech. Dedicated messengers from the exchange will deliver the messages back and forth, making it more convenient for users. Recently, Director Shen of the Construction Department believed that long-distance telephone only focused on the south of the Yangtze River, while the major cities in the north of the Yangtze River were still lacking. Expansion should be accelerated, poles and lines should be laid, and efforts should be made to proceed. He specially sent Technician Li Yangmeng to make practical plans and decided to connect Jiangdu, Gaoyou, Taixing, and Nantong from the Zhenjiang water line. It can be implemented in the shortest time, and it is expected that communication between the north and south of the Yangtze River will be possible after autumn.

Changshu Water Police Sentenced to Imprisonment for Transporting Opium

Pu Jinrong, a water police patrol officer stationed in Nantong, transported hundreds of pounds of opium through Baimao Port in this county earlier this month. He was discovered and intercepted by the local police team and sent to the county judicial office for investigation. In order to conclude the case as soon as possible, the county government sentenced Pu Jinrong to one year and six months in prison and fined him 2,500 yuan for the crime of selling opium on the 27th. Pu declared in court that he was dissatisfied and filed an appeal.

Resolution of the Election Fraud Case in the Chamber of Commerce

The county Chamber of Commerce here held a re-election of executive and supervisory committee members in October last year. Among them, half of the old executive committee members should have been removed by drawing lots in accordance with the regulations. Unexpectedly, when Wu Zhongying, a member of the Party Department, was drawing lots, a member of the money industry discovered on the spot that the drawing of lots was fraudulent because there were differences in length and thickness. Therefore, it was immediately revealed and all ballot papers were sealed and sent to the county government. However, the issue of re-election was shelved. Now the business of the association is still maintained by the old members. Chairman Pang Jiegong has submitted the above situation to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for explanation and has received a reply that there is nothing inappropriate. Therefore, the elected committee members are of course valid, and it is scheduled to elect standing committee members and chairman on March 1st.

Consolidation of the Public Security Bureau in Nantong County

Due to insufficient funding and numerous malpractices, more than 20 public security sub-bureaus in Nantong County have been consolidated. It was decided at the county administrative meeting to abolish all public security sub-bureaus. The provincial department has approved the establishment of seven sub-bureaus and six branch offices in the entire county, which will be implemented on March 1st.

Bribery Case of Private Sale of Drugs by a Pharmacy

Taihe Pharmacy on Nandajie in the city secretly sold and manufactured red pill drugs. The apprentice leaked the information to the outside and urgently bribed the police officer with 400 yuan to settle the matter. County Chief Cheng ordered Fu Qianzhi, the director of the Public Security Bureau, to thoroughly investigate the matter due to public outcry.

Opium Smugglers Intercepted in Yangzhou

Chen Rongtai, an opium smuggler from Luodian Lane, Yongsheng Street in the city, hired a small boat to privately transport nine large packages of opium (weighing about 500 to 600 taels) from Zhenjiang to Yangzhou. Unexpectedly, the matter was discovered by the Fifth Branch of the Public Security Bureau. Patrol Chief Wang Changze led police officers to investigate separately. At 9 pm on the 27th, Yang Qilai and Yang Zuoshi, the boatmen transporting the opium, were arrested outside Bianyi Gate and five packages of opium (weighing 300 taels) were seized. They were taken to the general bureau for interrogation.

Landlords Shot by Bandits in Gaoyou

Three bandits suddenly broke into the home of Dai Minglan, a farmer in Jizai Township in the second district of the county, and kicked open the back door. At that time, Dai was not asleep and woke up his family upon hearing the sound. They each held hoes, forks, and rakes to resist the bandits. Because the bandits were outnumbered, they planned to escape through the side door. Unexpectedly, Dai Minglan held a wooden stick and blocked their way. One of the bandits was extremely angry and shot Dai, hitting him in the waist. He fell to the ground and died immediately. The family has reported to the district office and transferred the report to the county government, requesting an order to strictly arrest them.

One Person Burned to Death in a Fire

Zhou Baoying's family, residents of Maben Town in the county, started a fire due to carelessness the night before. At that time, the wind helped the fire. Although the neighbors tried their best to put out the fire, it was ineffective. As a result, four houses were burned down. Zhou's young child was unable to be rescued due to the intense fire and was burned to death, which is also tragic.

Jiasan Jizheng Rice Shop Closed Down

Jizheng Rice Shop outside the West Gate has been open for more than 30 years. Its business is the best in the county. In recent years, it has suffered a lot of losses due to the impact of the rural economic bankruptcy. It suddenly closed down. Anjiu and other Qianzhhuang in the city owed the rice shop a debt of about 35,000 yuan. Representatives were immediately sent to file a lawsuit in the local court. Yesterday, the representatives of the Qianzhhuang were summoned by the court president, accompanied by Clerk Chen, and led the bailiffs to seal up and detain part of the shop's real estate, including 29 storefronts, the entire rice shop, rice factory, rice warehouse goods, and many other real estate properties, for auction and repayment.

Special Report

Impressions of the Economic Survey of Guangxi Province (V) Qian Jiaju

However, on the other hand, the development of highways is not without its negative effects. The first impact it has on the economic status of Guangxi Province is to aggravate the serious problem of Guangxi's foreign trade deficit. Once the highways are built, automobiles and gasoline have to be supplied from abroad. We only need to look at the report of the Guangxi Customs. The import of automobiles started in the ninth year of the Republic, with a value of only 8,918 customs taels. By the seventeenth year of the Republic, it suddenly jumped to 223,019 customs taels. 129,460 customs taels in the eighteenth year, and 25,702 customs taels in the twentieth year. The import of gasoline was only 153,393 gallons in the fifteenth year of the Republic, worth 54,218 customs taels. In the eighteenth year of the Republic, it suddenly increased to 449,412 gallons, worth 206,471 customs taels. In the twentieth year, it was 363,156 gallons, worth 233,713 customs taels. The huge increase in the import of automobiles and gasoline undoubtedly contributed to the increase in Guangxi's deficit. Second, the significance of highways in transportation is not comparable to that of railways or ships. The automobiles currently used in Guangxi have a load capacity of mostly less than 2.5 tons. In addition to facilitating travel, they are not only useless for transporting agricultural products, but also have little effect on transporting goods because the freight is too expensive and they cannot carry large quantities of goods. Therefore, except for a few items such as opium and foreign yarn that can be transported by highways, other goods cannot enjoy the benefits of highways. Third, it deepened the estrangement between the government and the people. There are three types of shares for the construction of highways in Guangxi. One is land shares, that is, wherever the highway passes, the people's land is confiscated according to its value as shares. However, the so-called "shares" are mostly not issued, and the land tax is still borne. The second is labor shares, that is, the conscription of people to build roads. In name, it is said to be paid 4 jiao a day, but in fact, only 1 or 2 jiao is often issued for food, and the remaining 2 jiao is used as labor shares. The third is road shares, that is, commercial shares. Although the name is free donation by merchants and civilians, it is actually a forced solicitation. From this, it can be seen that highways are completely built with the money and blood of the people. However, after the highways are built, farmers' ox carts and horse carts are not allowed to pass (because they are easy to damage the road surface). As a result, they have lost their inherent means of transportation. Farmers cannot afford to take cars. Most of the people who take cars are people with a little property or public officials. Whenever a car passes by, the dust rises high, and if they are slow to avoid it, they will be scolded immediately. Whenever we sit in the car and see the bitter faces of the farmers who dare to be angry but dare not speak, we always feel extremely sad. In addition, Guangxi also has a special phenomenon that is not seen in other provinces, that is, the extravagant life and arrogant atmosphere of the drivers. Their monthly income is more abundant than that of an ordinary county magistrate. The salary of a county magistrate in Guangxi is usually 140 yuan, but the income of an ordinary driver is at least 80 yuan, and many earn up to 200 yuan (the salary is only 40 or 50 yuan, but the extra income is extremely abundant). The special status of drivers is formed because the demand for drivers exceeds the supply after the large-scale highway construction, and because Guangxi has no training for this type of talent, it has to be recruited from Guangzhou. Scarcity makes it valuable. Once they arrive in the remote Guangxi, they will naturally act like the kings of Yelang and treat customers or ordinary people as emperors. We once talked to Chairman Huang about this situation. Chairman Huang said that they had heard about it for a long time and are now planning to set up a driver training school to recruit junior high school graduates for training. If they can do this, we believe it is the most effective way.

Although highways are not as important as railways in terms of economy, they have their own value in terms of transportation and military affairs. To remedy the shortcomings of highways in transportation, we believe that first, farmers should be allowed to use ox carts and horse carts. However, in order to avoid damaging the road surface, it may be stipulated that ox cart wheels should have a certain width or size, or that the wheels should be covered with rubber. In recent years, the price of rubber has plummeted. If the government purchases it in large quantities and resells it to farmers, we are confident that farmers can afford it. Second, the government can purchase more heavy-duty trucks. The load capacity of American trucks has reached 10 tons. This is naturally not possible on the current soft sandy road surface in Guangxi. However, if the road surface and bridges are slightly improved, using 4 or 5-ton trucks will not cause them to sink. The Construction Department may use the road maintenance fee income to purchase more of these trucks for the transportation of goods. The freight should also be fair and low to reduce the cost of goods. If these two measures are implemented, highways will not be "just for travel" as they are now.

Local News

German Ambassador's Reply to the Chamber of Commerce Confirms No Recognition of the Puppet Manchukuo

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce received a telegram from the German Ambassador, Dr. Trautmann, yesterday: "To the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Your telegram has been read. Two days ago, a telegram released by a semi-official German news agency was published in Chinese newspapers. This telegram is sufficient to prove that the rumors you mentioned are false. You can make satisfactory publicity." Trautmann, January.

Temporary Martial Law Today

Wen Hongen, director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, received a phone call from the municipal government yesterday afternoon ordering the implementation of temporary martial law from 6:00 a.m. to 6:00 p.m. on March 1 (today). After receiving the order, Director Wen immediately ordered all districts to comply.

Interview with Chu Minyi

According to the Central News Agency, Chu Minyi, secretary of the Executive Yuan, arrived in Shanghai by night express train from Nanjing at 7:30 a.m. yesterday. Chen Shaokuan, the Minister of the Navy, and Gan Naiguang, the vice-minister, arrived in Shanghai with Chu. After getting off the train, Chu returned to his residence on Avenue Albert and then went to the Sino-French School to handle school affairs. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited the school and asked about the progress of the Xinjiang Construction Planning Committee. The following is a record of his interview:

Developing New Provinces

The central government has already begun to develop the Northwest region. It is well known that the Northwest provinces have vast land and sparse population, and are rich in minerals. Therefore, developing the Northwest is the only way out for our country. Xinjiang is located in the west, with vast land and abundant resources, which is the best among all provinces. People who care about national affairs have successively gone to the area to conduct inspections, and they all believe that the development of Xinjiang is urgent. Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan was aware of this and ordered me to prepare for the Xinjiang Construction Planning Committee. After being appointed, I sent letters to various departments to select and appoint those familiar with the situation in the province to serve as members of the committee. Twenty-five people, including Li Jingcong and Tang Kesan, have been appointed as members. Li Tang and others know more about the situation in Xinjiang, so they should be able to express their opinions on the planning of Xinjiang's construction. It has now been decided to hold the first meeting in Nanjing within the next week. After that, meetings will be held every week or every two weeks, and the contributions will be presented to the competent authorities for implementation as much as possible. The committee is under the Executive Yuan. The meetings are convened by me, and the issues discussed are limited to construction, such as developing new provincial transportation, developing mineral resources, and implementing education. Political issues will also be studied. There are no formal reports on the war in the province. The central government has not yet received reliable reports on the situation in Kashi, southern Xinjiang, due to inconvenient transportation and difficult communication. The news published in various newspapers is all foreign telegrams, and there is bound to be considerable manipulation among them. Therefore, the construction of transportation in the new province is the only important task, and it cannot be delayed for even a moment.

Panchen's Southern Tour

Chu continued, "In addition to handling school affairs and attending the board of directors of the Sino-French Pharmacy, I came to Shanghai this time to contact Wang Yiting, Wen Lanting, and others about welcoming the Panchen Lama to Shanghai. Vice-Chairman Zhao Pilian of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission and others hosted a banquet for the Panchen Lama in Nanjing last night, and I was also present. During the banquet, the Panchen Lama mentioned the famous scenic spots in the south of the Yangtze River and expressed his intention to visit them. The Panchen Lama left Tibet for the south in the first year of the Republic of China and has been to Nanjing three times. However, he only visited Hangzhou and other places once in the thirteenth year of the Republic of China. He decided to leave Nanjing for Shanghai around March 20 and stay for a short time before going to Hangzhou for a temporary residence. He also plans to lecture several times in Shanghai, Hangzhou, and other places. After the weather warms up, he will go to Qinghai and other places. As for the date when the central government specially sends Ambassador Huang Musong to Tibet, there is no definite date yet."

Silver Issue

Chu also said, "The silver price issue will be submitted to the Central Political Council for discussion this morning, and there will be a concrete decision. Raising the price of silver will be detrimental to our country. The central government is paying close attention to this and will organize a special committee to conduct a serious study. The issue of currency reorganization will also be studied in detail. As for the cases decided by the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Committee, they have been sorted out and implemented separately. The case of reforming the provincial system is also in progress. The rumors that the central government will order Jiangsu, Anhui, and other provinces to conduct trials first are not true."

China and Foreign Countries Attach Importance to Raising Silver Prices

Roosevelt Telegraphed the Consul General in Shanghai to Investigate and Reply

Foreign Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed Roosevelt Advocating Caution

International Trade Bureau Said It Was Detrimental to Us

Since the Shanghai Banking Association telegraphed US President Roosevelt to protest the policy of raising silver prices, as the telegram was not delivered through diplomatic channels, Roosevelt did not reply. However, according to reliable sources, Roosevelt has indeed attached great importance to this and telegraphed the US commercial agencies to investigate. At the same time, the local foreign chambers of commerce also telegraphed Roosevelt, asking him to handle it with caution. The details are recorded separately below:

Consuls Sent Orders to Investigate

After receiving the protest telegram from the Shanghai Banking Association stating that raising silver prices would be detrimental to our country, Roosevelt telegraphed Arnold C. Kuhlman, the US Commercial Counselor at No. 3 Guangdong Road, and Consul General Clarence E. Gauss yesterday to investigate our country's financial situation, price index, and commercial realities, and whether there would be any harm to China after the silver price raising policy is implemented in the future. After receiving the telegram, the Consul General and the Commercial Counselor formulated forms and ordered experts to conduct detailed investigations to the relevant agencies and Chinese and foreign banks. Arnold and Clarence are very familiar with the situation in China and are regarded by Americans as "China hands." Roosevelt attaches great importance to their reports. It is estimated that the US standard and steps for raising silver prices must wait until the reports of the two arrive in the US and are studied before they can be decided.

Foreign Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed Roosevelt Advocating Caution

According to the Continental News, the Shanghai Foreign Chamber of Commerce held a general affairs committee meeting on Friday last week and resolved to telegraph President Roosevelt, asking him to carefully consider the impact of the silver system legislation proposed by the US Congress on China. The telegram was sent out last night (27th) and read: "The Shanghai Foreign Chamber of Commerce, which has representatives from 12 countries, respectfully requests Your Excellency to consider the impact of any silver system legislation on China. We believe that this legislation should be limited to the price of silver in the United States and should not involve the world price of silver. What is necessary for China's prosperity is that the price of silver must increase in accordance with the increase in general prices. China has been able to avoid the major impact of the world economic crisis due to the low price of silver, while other countries have used high-priced round currency units, resulting in harmful results, and have reduced the value of the currency as a remedy. Imports to China must be paid for by its exports or loans to China, otherwise Chinese silver will flow out continuously. The increase in the price of silver will cause land prices and commodity prices to plummet, and it will be necessary to prohibit the export of silver or impose an export tax on silver. Then China will be on a managed round currency basis. "This telegram was sent out last night, so no reply has been received yet.

Lin Kanghou Said He Would Listen to the Government

According to a telegram from Nanjing, the news that the Central Political Council has approved the silver agreement has been passed. A reporter from Shin Shi News visited Lin Kanghou, the secretary-general of the Banking Association, and asked for his opinion on the approval of the agreement. According to Lin, the Banking Association had previously telegraphed the central government, requesting a temporary delay in approving the silver agreement. This is the opinion of the banking industry colleagues. However, whether to adopt it or not is up to the government's own decision. The banking industry has no opinion to express. However, since the government has approved the agreement, it will inevitably have appropriate countermeasures when the US raises silver prices in the future. We can only wait and see the development of the US policy and re-determine the response policy at any time.

Last Year's Silver Exports Increased Significantly

According to the International Trade Bureau, our country is a silver-using country. Silver is the lifeblood of our country. US President Roosevelt is implementing a monetary policy to lower the price of the US dollar and raise the price of silver. This policy has a gradual outflow crisis for our country's silver. In recent years, our country's rural areas have gone bankrupt, prices have fallen, foreign goods have flooded the market, and the trade deficit has increased year by year. Silver outflows are countless. According to customs reports, the value of silver exported from our country in the 21st year of the Republic of China was 57,645,491 yuan in national currency. By last year, it had increased to 94,288,936 yuan, of which exports to the United States accounted for more than 70% of the total. If the US policy is implemented this time, it will be even more unfavorable to the people's livelihood and economy, and the trade deficit and silver exports will be even more considerable. The following is a statistic of silver exports from our country to various countries in the past two years:

Country Name 21st Year of the Republic of China 22nd Year of the Republic of China

Annam 1,246 196,020

HSBC Bank Annual Meeting Discussion

The Zi Lin Bao (North-China Daily News) reported that at the HSBC Bank's annual shareholders meeting held in Hong Kong last Saturday and Sunday, Chairman Peel mentioned the silver issue in his speech. He stated that three years ago, the chairman at the time mentioned the status of silver and hoped that all relevant governments would cease any plans that would worsen its status. We still hold this view, believing that government intervention aimed at artificially raising silver prices in China could only be harmful. For this reason, we do not approve of the silver agreement reached at the London World Economic Conference. This sets a precedent for attempting to manage the supply of silver. Although the amount involved is relatively small, its impact on silver prices is also very subtle. It seems that this will continue to be the case in the future. However, the establishment of an international agreement that regulates artificial markets and restricts the free operation of supply and demand is enough to encourage silver speculators. The decline in currency values worldwide has caused silver prices to rise relative to various currencies. At the same time, the prices of Chinese export goods have also risen accordingly. China is gradually needing to export silver to pay for its import goods, which is an ominous sign. We can better understand the situation by briefly looking at the following figures: In the seven years leading up to the end of 1930, India and China together consumed an average of approximately 66% of the world's silver supply, which is approximately 200 million ounces per year. In 1931, consumption fell to 116 million ounces, and in 1932, it fell to 52 million ounces. In 1933, India consumed approximately 10 million ounces, while China's silver exports exceeded imports by 15 million ounces. From this, it can be seen that those who previously consumed two-thirds of the world's silver supply have now left the silver market. Although the world's silver production has fallen from an average of approximately 240 million ounces per year to 163 million ounces, the total supply last year was still as high as 273 million ounces. This is not much less than the average supply in the past seven years. Therefore, there are now more than 150 million ounces of silver that no one is concerned about, and they are mostly in the hands of speculators. I believe that you are well aware that the current unstable state is caused by the possibility of the sudden adoption of government plans, which can completely change the situation overnight and put merchants in a very difficult position, and greatly increase the burden on bankers engaged in foreign exchange business, and so on.

Public Commemoration of Wu Tiyun Scheduled

To be Held on April 1st

Resolution by the Sponsors Meeting Yesterday

After the Central Committee member Wu Chaoshu passed away in Hong Kong, Wu's relatives and friends, as well as people from across the country and friendly nations, were all saddened. Legislative Yuan President Sun Ke and former Minister of Railways Ye Gongchuo, who had a deep friendship with Commissioner Wu during his lifetime, initiated the holding of a memorial meeting for Commissioner Wu and solicited sponsors from all walks of life. It is now reported that the number of people who have agreed to participate as sponsors has reached several hundred. The sponsors' meeting was held at 2:00 PM yesterday in the East Hall on the ninth floor of the YMCA at Eight Immortals Bridge to discuss the arrangements for the memorial meeting and to appoint a preparatory committee to immediately begin preparations.

Attendees

The sponsors who attended yesterday, representing groups, included Huang Zaoxiong representing the Municipal Education Association, Yu Zhenhui representing the Municipal Agricultural Association, Lu Danlin representing the Road Association, Tao Leqin representing the Shanghai Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association, Zhang Yichen and Hu Fengxiang representing the First Special District Citizens' Association, Xu Xingchu representing the Chinese International Society, Jiang Yiping representing the Lawyers Association, and Huang Renzhi representing the Shanghai Local Association. Chairman's Report

At the beginning of the meeting, all the sponsors stood up to observe a three-minute silence for Commissioner Wu. Then, Chairman Ye Gongchuo reported, stating that Commissioner Wu's learning and knowledge had always been admired by his colleagues, and his handling of foreign affairs was particularly praised in diplomatic circles. He had contributed greatly to the party and the country. Unfortunately, he suddenly fell ill and passed away in Hong Kong. This is a loss for China. Everyone was shocked and saddened by this sad news. It is the intention of the colleagues that there is a need for a centralized expression regarding the passing of Commissioner Wu, as it can show mourning and make an impression on society. Therefore, I and President Sun Zhesheng initiated the holding of a memorial meeting and notified all parties to solicit opinions. Now, over thirty central government departments and provincial governments, as well as over ten local party headquarters, forty-odd groups, and over four hundred and fifty individuals have joined. Commissioner Wu will be buried on March 13th, and large-scale memorial services will be held in Guangzhou and Hong Kong. Mrs. Wu will come to Shanghai from the north immediately after Commissioner Wu's burial, and the memorial meeting will be held at that time. However, the holding of the memorial meeting is only of a temporary nature. We should formulate permanent memorial measures, one being to establish a scholarship fund, and the other being to establish a school. These two matters are already complicated, so we will determine them after Mrs. Wu comes to Shanghai and we solicit her opinions. Now, we will ask you to discuss the methods for holding the memorial meeting.

Resolution Methods

After the Chairman's report, the discussion began, and the following was resolved: (1) Memorial meeting proposal: It was decided that the meeting would be held at 2:00 PM on April 1st at the Shanghai Municipal Government Auditorium. (2) Publication of a commemorative album: It was decided that the preparatory committee would compile and print it. The order of compilation would be: 1. Commendation certificate from the National Government; 2. Portrait of Commissioner Wu; 3. Calligraphy of Commissioner Wu; 4. Biography of Commissioner Wu. (3) Establishment of the Tiyun Scholarship and preparation for the Tiyun Memorial School: Deferred for discussion. (4) Funding for the memorial meeting: It was decided that the Zhongshan Culture and Education Center would temporarily provide funds, and the sponsors would share the costs in the future. (5) Articles of Association of the Preparatory Committee: It was decided to amend and pass them. (6) Nomination of Preparatory Committee members: It was decided to nominate Cai Yuanpei, Li Zhaohuan, Huang Renzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Shi Liangcai, Lin Kanghou, Sun Zhesheng, Ye Gongchuo, Wu Tiecheng, Wang Jingwei, Zhang Jingjiang, Xue Ziliang, Zheng Shaojue, Ma Xingqiao, Kong Yongzhi, Yang Cangbai, Chu Minyi, Liu Yazi, Li Liejun, Zhang Zhiben, Du Yuesheng, Lao Jingxiu, Guo Shun, Tao Lvqian, Chen Choushuo, Zhang Huichang, Fu Bingchang, Li Dachao representing the Shanghai Municipal Government, Lin Meiyan representing the Municipal Party Headquarters, Tang Baoshu representing the Ministry of Communications, Zhu Shaoping representing the Municipal Gazetteer Office, and representatives from the Shanghai Guangzhao Public Association and the Guangdong Shanghai Association, totaling thirty-three people.

Charity Federation Requests Reduction of Land Value Tax for Charity Organizations

The Shanghai Charity Federation recently investigated the Municipal Finance Bureau's collection of land value tax, which was first implemented in the areas of South Shanghai, Zhabei, and Pudong. The Federation believes that most of its funds come from land income. Once the land value tax is implemented, the source of funds for charity organizations will inevitably be reduced, which will greatly affect the future of charitable undertakings. Yesterday, it submitted a petition to the Municipal Government and the Municipal Finance Bureau, along with two copies of the property list, requesting that, in addition to the exemptions permitted by regulations, the remaining tax be reduced by half.

French Female Aviator Hirth Did Not Arrive in Shanghai Last Night

Departed from Hong Kong Yesterday Morning with Bad Weather Along the Way

French Consulate Immediately Sent Telegrams to Various Places for Inquiry Yesterday

Learned Last Night That She Encountered Fog and Returned to Shantou to Land

French female aviator Hirth, who is making her second transcontinental flight between Paris and Tokyo in an airplane manufactured by the Hispano-Suiza factory, encountered setbacks along the way, but her ambition has not diminished. She flew from Hanoi to Hong Kong the day before yesterday and departed from Hong Kong yesterday morning to come to Shanghai, scheduled to arrive here at 1:00 PM yesterday. However, as of last night, there was no news. All parties were quite concerned about the safety of the lady.

Now that the news has been confirmed that she landed in Shantou due to fog, people are relieved. The details are recorded separately below.

Airplane Model

The airplane that Ms. Hirth is flying this time is larger than the one she flew to China last time. The airplane is a Breguet land-based aircraft No. 330 produced by the Hispano-Suiza aircraft factory (translated as the Swiss Company), with a 650-horsepower engine. It flies quite fast, estimated to travel 230 kilometers per hour. The airplane's designation is (Fakfm). It only takes six hours to travel from Hong Kong to Shanghai.

Long Wait Without Arrival

Yesterday, the local French Consulate received news that Ms. Hirth had departed from Hong Kong with her assistant Brax at 7:15 AM yesterday morning to come to Shanghai. The journey is 700 miles and it was estimated that she would arrive here around 1:00 PM. Therefore, representatives from all relevant parties, such as Security Chief Yang Hu, Special Section Chief Wang Chengzhi, led a small platoon of motorcycle machine gun security team to protect the airfield. In addition, those who came to welcome her included Aviation Association Secretary-General Lin Wojiang, French Consul-General Melia, Consul Gu A'fa, French Concession Police Chief Faber, French Association representative Wu Dingnai, US Air Force Captain Fulu, as well as French Concession Political Department Director Shandoyang, and many Chinese and French gentlemen and ladies, all went to Hongqiao Airport to welcome her. At the same time, the Public Security Bureau Passport Inspection Office also sent Yao Changzhen and Zhang Feifan to the airport to prepare to inspect entry passports and whether there were any contraband goods, etc. However, the welcomers waited until 4:40 PM and still did not see the airplane arrive in Shanghai. They called the French Consulate and other relevant parties to inquire, but did not receive any reports about Ms. Hirth. Therefore, the welcomers became impatient and returned to their residences to rest one after another.

Poor Weather

Yesterday, according to reports received from Hongqiao Airport, the weather in various ports in South China between Hangzhou and Hong Kong was quite bad. Based on this situation, it can be inferred that Ms. Hirth did not arrive in Shanghai after departing from Hong Kong yesterday morning, undoubtedly because she was blocked by bad weather. However, there was no news as to where she landed in the middle of the journey.

No News

Last night, various Chinese and foreign circles telegraphed the French Consulate to inquire about news. The French Consulate also telegraphed Fuzhou, Xiamen, and other places to inquire, but there was no trace of the airplane. There was no news. It is said that the airplane Ms. Hirth was traveling in did not have a radio, so all parties were extremely concerned about the lady's safety.

Returned to Shantou

Havas News Agency, Shantou, 28th Dispatch: Famous French female aviator, Ms. Hirth, flew from Hong Kong to Shanghai. Because she encountered fog in the middle of the journey and could not identify the route, she was forced to return 100 kilometers north of Xiamen. After noon, she landed in Shantou. Once the weather improves, she still intends to fly to Shanghai.

Commodity Inspection Bureau Convened Tea Merchants Meeting Yesterday

Crackdown on Toxic Colored Tea Leaves

Use of Non-Toxic Colorants

Since the Ministry of Industry's Commodity Inspection Bureau received the French government's ban on the import of colored toxic tea in 1932, considering that this matter concerned a large export of the country's agricultural products, if implemented, it would greatly impact international trade. Therefore, Chief Technician Zhou of the Bureau has been engaged in researching non-toxic colorants and has now invented them. After trial production and testing, they were very satisfied. Therefore, at 2:00 PM yesterday, they convened a conversation with Chinese and foreign tea merchants and requested tea merchants to use this non-toxic colorant and announced five measures. The details are recorded separately below.

Attendees

Those who attended yesterday, in addition to Commodity Inspection Bureau Director Cai Wuji and Tea Inspection Section Chemical Experiment Group Technician Zhou Zhenjun, included Yu Jinming of the Shanghai Tea Industry Association, Tao Zhensheng of the Shanghai Foreign Tea Industry Association, Tang Zhenxian, Tang Bingchen, and Dong Lai of China Tea Company, Yu Qintai of Yili Tea Company, Zhu Bogen of Yongxiang Tea Company, Hong Xinyuan and Hong Binxing of Wanyuan Tea Company, Piao Qiaosheng of Xiehe Foreign Company (Nicholson P.), Qiaopo (C.L. Chopdn) of Tongfu Foreign Company, Tang Bingxi of Yingfaxing, Wang Chunrong of Wanchengyu, Zheng Jianyuan of Yuanfengrun Tea Company, and Shan Huapu of Yongxinglong Tea Company, totaling over thirty representatives.

Trial Process

Yesterday, Director Cai Wuji gave a speech, the general idea being: The significance and implementation methods of the Bureau convening Chinese and foreign tea merchants today to discuss the implementation of changing to non-toxic yellow colorants. (1) The Bureau has been engaged in prohibiting the export of toxic colorant tea leaves since receiving an order from the Ministry of Industry last year. This matter is extremely important to the foreign trade of green tea in our country. The urgent need to prohibit such toxic colorants is one of the important missions of the Bureau's inspection policy, and it will be implemented before other countries make any expressions. (2) However, regarding the measures received by the Bureau last year, it was quite difficult to implement them in terms of timing and substitutes. Later, at the request of Chinese and foreign tea merchants, the Bureau requested the Ministry of Industry to allow a one-year grace period, and to implement them after the new tea was on the market this year. The Ministry of Industry approved this and notified all Chinese and foreign tea merchants last year. (3) In order to implement the Ministry's order and solve the difficulties of tea merchants, the Bureau specially spent a long period of time last year, with the Chemical Experiment Department designating Chief Technician Zhou to engage in the trial production of non-toxic yellow pigments. Fortunately, it has been completed in a very short time. Chief Technician Zhou has drafted a separate report on the advantages and disadvantages of toxic and non-toxic yellow pigments and the process of their creation, which can be consulted by everyone present. (4) The cost of the newly invented colorant is three-tenths stronger than the old toxic colorant. The two together are two-thirds stronger. The estimated cost of non-toxic tea colorant from numbers one to five is about twice as high per pound, while the difference between numbers six to eight is negligible. If there is a large amount of manufacturing and common management, the price will be lower. (5) There are two important issues for discussion today: (A) How to manufacture and sell the non-toxic pigments invented by the Bureau; (B) How to implement and supervise tea merchants in all localities to uniformly change to the new pigments, and notify the Shanghai Tea Merchant Association and the Foreign Tea Industry Association. Last year, the Bureau also sent personnel to various counties in Anhui Province and Shaoxing and Wenzhou to promote the pigments. However, it is deeply feared that a small number of tea merchants will outwardly agree but inwardly disobey, so tea merchants must jointly implement the measure. If there is a surplus from the sale of non-toxic colorants by the Bureau, it will be used for public research and public undertakings in the tea industry.

Crackdown Measures

The Bureau also notified Chinese and foreign tea companies and tea houses of five measures for using non-toxic colorants and inspection: (1) Registering tea factories: In order for the Bureau to facilitate guidance and supervision, the Shanghai local tea companies will be registered first. The registration period is approximately before February and March of this year. (2) Specifying colorants: Article 12 of the regulations promulgated by France on July 7, 1932, regarding the import of colored tea into French territories, states that "Green tea that is mixed with various teas and colored with indigo, turmeric, talc, or gypsum is not prohibited." Indigo is commonly used by merchants, so there is not much problem with blue. The use of turmeric has a slightly astringent taste, which is actually obstructive. The Bureau has been engaged in research, and substitutes for light yellow and deep yellow have been completed. Substitutes for deep yellow such as Three Fish have also been trial-produced and will soon be distributed to various tea companies for trial use. There will also be results. Therefore, regarding coloring colorants, those with existing products available will be designated. Those without equivalent products available will be made by the Bureau, and the colorants will be announced. (3) Issuing a notice to submit tea samples: When tea houses and local tea companies transport or produce each type of tea leaf and distribute tea samples to various foreign companies, they must also submit a copy to the Bureau for preliminary inspection. Once a prohibited coloring is discovered, the Bureau will notify the tea houses and foreign companies to prohibit sales, as a precautionary measure to avoid unexpected disturbances. This measure will be implemented when the new tea is on the market this year. (4) Registering the capacity of colored tea this year: The old tea that has not been sold before the new tea is on the market next year is customarily blended and sold in the new tea, which is bound to mix the spurious with the genuine, making it extremely difficult to crack down. It is planned to order Chinese and foreign tea merchants to register the existing green tea with the Bureau within a certain period this year. At the same time, personnel will be dispatched to thoroughly investigate and prevent concealment. Those who are found to have toxic colorants when the registered green tea is sold out will be strictly cracked down in accordance with the regulations. (5) Requesting the Ministry to notify tea-producing provinces and tea merchants manufacturing green tea to pay attention to colorants: Now that the Bureau's colorants have been decided, a request has been submitted to notify all green tea manufacturers to pay attention.

Leading Inspection

In order for Chinese and foreign tea merchants to understand the newly created non-toxic yellow colorant, the Bureau specially used water to brew toxic colorant tea leaves and non-toxic colorant tea leaves separately in tea bowls to observe the color depth and tea quality and taste. As a result, all tea merchants were satisfied. After the inspection, the meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

New Director of the Maritime Administration Bureau, Peng Hu, Took Office Yesterday

After Zhu Yaoting, Director of the Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, was transferred to the position of Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Bureau, the Ministry of Communications appointed Peng Hu, Deputy Director of the General Affairs Section of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, to replace him. Appointed Staff

After Peng arrived at the Bureau, the former secretary and the chiefs of the first and second sections had resigned and gone to Zhejiang with Director Zhu to take on their new positions. Therefore, Chen Baoyan was appointed as secretary, Chou Lunjie as chief of the first section, and He Daoyun as chief of the second section.

Expressed Opinions

According to Peng, he will not make changes to the internal staff in order to maintain skilled personnel, but will strive to increase efficiency in handling affairs. He also said that he is not good at publicity and will devote his efforts to planning and engaging in practical work. Peng expressed that there were not many achievements in the shipping industry in the past, so it is necessary to urgently seek to save our declining shipping industry. Peng's courtesy name is Shinian, and he is from Liuyang, Hunan. He has a Master of Arts in Political Science from Stanford University in the United States and has served as Secretary of the Ministry of Communications, Director of the Central Training Department, and Deputy Director of the General Affairs Section of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Petitions for Correction of Tianjin's Illegal Collection of Teeth Tax

Fruit Industry Representatives Go to Tianjin to Petition

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted a petition to the Beiping Political Affairs Branch of the Executive Yuan and the Hebei Provincial Government, stating that the teeth tax originated in the Qing Dynasty and has been continued since the Republic of China. Its nature is a business tax levied on specially licensed businesses. Therefore, the teeth tax post and the tax are often mentioned together. The target of taxation is shops, not goods, which is different from the Likin tax. The tax amount is usually determined by the remoteness of the area, the size of the shop, and its grade. Therefore, each teeth tax post, even in prosperous areas, and according to the type of business, those who should receive the first-class teeth tax post pay up to several yuan. Among them, there are examples of long-term teeth tax posts that are limited to being renewed every twenty years. Such a situation is clearly verifiable. The scope of teeth tax post registration and tax payment is limited to tooth rows. The so-called tooth row refers to the tooth brokers who buy and sell on behalf of customers. Self-purchase and self-sale, those who do not operate by collecting commissions, are of course not within the scope of teeth tax. However, the interim regulations on teeth tax formulated by Tianjin Municipality are completely different from this. Article 3 of its regulations states that the teeth tax rate should not exceed 3% of the price of goods and should be borne by both the buyer and seller, with the buyer bearing 2% and the seller bearing 1% in principle. According to this method, it is clearly a goods tax rather than a teeth tax post. Therefore, the teeth tax collection office levies tax on each batch of goods transported from other places or from other places to Tianjin, and issues tax bills. The text printed on the tax bill states, "This tax bill is issued so that the bureaus and checkpoints along the way can check the freight bills and stamp them for release without delay or obstruction. If there are any discrepancies such as concealed goods or mismatched freight bills, they will be detained and punished without leniency." This is clearly a Likin checkpoint. This is by no means a so-called teeth tax post. This is the actual situation of the current teeth tax in Tianjin, which violates the national government's order to abolish Likin. Furthermore, in terms of the Tianjin fresh goods teeth tax, it is divided into two major markets, located in the Xihe and Yuhe areas. There has never been a tooth row in the Haihe area. It is of a passing-through or self-purchasing and self-selling nature. In September of the 17th year of the Republic of China, the Tianjin authorities recruited merchants to contract the teeth tax and added the Haihe area. The contractor Zhao Yuqi won the bid. Tianjin merchants protested for three months because there had never been a teeth tax in the Haihe area. Zhao withdrew from the contract. Finally, the Tianjin Fresh and Dried Fruits Industry Guild requested that the Haihe be exempted from the teeth tax and changed to an annual apportionment of 37,000 yuan for all fresh fruits, regardless of north or south. In September of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the guild's contract expired. In February of this year, a new merchant, Chen Xizhi, won the bid with 150,800 yuan, five times the previous amount. After taking over, he recruited more than 300 teeth tax clerks and set up offices along the way to check everywhere. Regardless of whether they were carrying goods on their shoulders or in small quantities, even if they were not going through the tooth row, they had to be assessed and taxed. They also intercepted and taxed goods passing through the Haihe area. If their demands were not met, they would detain the goods and arrest people to show their power. Two batches of sugarcane and tangerines from Shanghai to Tianjin have been detained. After the two batches of goods were detained, the Shanghai Fruit and Local Goods Industry Guild sent a telegram to the Mayor of Tianjin with some statements. The Mayor of Tianjin replied in a telegram that he did not mention whether the teeth tax was levied according to the price of the goods, whether the goods should be taxed once they arrived, and a tax bill issued, so that the bureaus and checkpoints along the way could check and stamp them, whether each was a teeth tax, regardless of whether they were carrying goods on their shoulders or in small quantities, whether they were going through the tooth row, and whether officials should be sent to intercept and detain goods passing through the Haihe area. He only attributed this matter to the replacement of contractors and the guild's failure to contract. This avoided the legal point of contention and focused on the defense of trivial matters. Shanghai fruit merchants, under these circumstances, believed that the municipal government had no way to appeal and requested to appeal to the higher-level competent authorities. The chairman of the Shanghai Fruit and Local Goods Industry Guild, Cai Run, requested to attend the meeting. As mentioned above, the teeth tax should not be levied on each item. The Haihe area has always been without tooth brokers. Where do the tooth brokers come from? This is especially the focus of Tianjin fresh fruit merchants. Respectfully, a special representative was sent to bring the petition to the front to petition, hoping that it would be approved that the collection of fresh goods teeth tax in Tianjin violates the tax law and contradicts the Likin abolition plan, and that it should be corrected.

Jianghai Customs Ordered to Establish Machinery-Made Goods Exhibition Hall

Opening Ceremony Scheduled for the Afternoon of the 5th

Kong Xiangxi Decides to Come to Shanghai in Person to Attend

Jianghai Customs was ordered by the Ministry of Finance to establish a permanent exhibition hall for machine-made goods for exhibition purposes. Preparations have now been completed, and the opening ceremony is scheduled for 2:30 PM on the 5th of this month. The details are as follows:

Ordered to Establish

The Jianghai Customs Superintendent of Customs was instructed by the Ministry of Finance to establish an exhibition hall for machine-made goods. All machine-made goods produced by Chinese and foreign merchants within the Jianghai Customs area of China, which have been registered by the Ministry of Finance and recognized as tax-free exports, shall be exhibited so that merchants can understand the various tax-free export goods and not be deceived. The address is on the third floor of Jianghai Customs on the Bund of Sanma Road, on the west end of the south side.

Preparations Completed

The machine-made goods exhibition hall on the south side of the third floor of Jianghai Customs has been prepared and is ready. The entrance of the exhibition hall is marked with the Chinese and Western characters "Machine-Made Goods Exhibition Hall" to welcome visitors. Wooden cabinets are placed in the room, with glass on all sides, divided into three layers. Various machine-made goods are displayed in the cabinets. A wooden table is placed at the entrance for visitors to sign in. Various machine-made goods patterns are hung on the wall, and the layout is very unique.

Classified Exhibition

The products of each factory on display are classified, such as silk fabrics, cotton fabrics, woolen fabrics, cosmetics, electrical materials, woolen piece goods, canned foods, porcelain, Luzai goods, various toys, towels, socks, hats, umbrellas, etc. are all complete, and the names of the goods and the producing factories are marked for permanent display. Visitors are not charged any fees. The daily hours are the same as the office hours of Jianghai Customs.

Scheduled Opening

The exhibition hall is scheduled to open at 2:30 PM on March 5. Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi has decided to attend in person, deliver the opening speech, and invite people from all walks of life to visit. "Our Customs has specially set up a machine-made goods exhibition hall to permanently display the products of all factories within the Jianghai Customs area that enjoy the treatment of machine-made Western-style goods, for exhibition purposes. The opening ceremony is scheduled to be held at 2:30 PM on March 5, 23rd year of the Republic of China. You are respectfully invited to come and give your guidance. Sincerely ordered by the Jianghai Customs Superintendent of Customs."

Lianglu Joint Water and Land Transportation to be Implemented Starting Today

Land Route Connects Long-Distance Buses in Danyang

Water Route Connects Ships at Jiashan Station

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations will officially handle the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Zhen-Danyang-Jintan-Liyang long-distance bus joint transportation and the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Zhouzhuang-Jiashan joint transportation starting today. Both railways' transportation departments notified all stations to comply. The details are as follows:

Beijing-Shanghai Railway

The Zhen-Danyang-Jintan-Liyang long-distance bus route starts from Zhenjiang via Danyang to Jintan and reaches Liyang. After signing a joint transportation contract with the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, it will be implemented starting today. The railway bureau will use Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Changzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, and Shanghai as six stations. Before the company completes the entire route, it will temporarily sell joint transportation tickets at Jintan Station first. Other stations will gradually expand as needed. Both parties will use Danyang as the connecting station. The railway bureau will charge according to the grade specified on the ticket. The company does not divide into grades. In addition to passenger cars, the company also prepares a towing vehicle to pick up and drop off joint transportation vehicles and packages.

Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo

Wu Qing Ji Shipping Company operates the Zhouzhuang-Jiashan line in Wujiang County, passing through Lili, Luxu, Xutang, and other places. After signing a joint transportation contract with the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, it is scheduled to be implemented starting today. It has been decided to handle passenger joint transportation first. Cargo and luggage will be suspended for the time being. The railway bureau will use Shanghai North Station, Fengjing, Jiaxing, Hangzhou Nanxing Bridge, and other six stations. The shipping bureau will use Xutang, Luxu, Lili, Zhouzhuang, and other four ports. Both parties will use Jiashan as the connecting station to sell joint transportation passenger tickets, limited to second, third, and fourth class. The shipping bureau's tickets are not divided into grades.
