— Meng Zhao

Everyone knows: Facts are the most eloquent! He and his patriotic female student wife always felt that their married life was disharmonious! He is a modern Western-dressed young man, and she is a patriotic woman who does not like to dress up and loves thrift.

He mistakenly believed that girls in the city are invariably fond of vanity and extravagance! When they were first married, in order to please his wife, he always bought imported cosmetics as tribute when he came back from work! He smiled at his wife and said:

"My Love. Do you like this?" She did not step forward, nor did she pay attention. A wisp of her heart……was thinking, "Why do Chinese young men have to be so shameless｜to flatter foreigners? No, maybe he is manipulating the domesticating power of women! Alas!"

After a while, she said solemnly to her husband:

"Chinese people, please speak Chinese! Chinese people, please use Chinese goods. This degenerate thing! Please... give it to the modern girl you love!"

When he heard this, he couldn't help but feel anger rising from his heart. "Thinking that this woman is too unappreciative, not only can't she get sweet happiness in the early days of her marriage, but she is suffering from a burst of anger that has nowhere to vent! Their goals are different, their paths are incompatible, damn it! He decided to divorce her, see how she is?" After a few days, the two sides were indeed involved in a lawsuit｜It was his initiative to ask the judge to allow the divorce. The judge summoned her to inquire about the facts of the dispute. She stated it eloquently, and finally｜Also said, who is right and who is wrong? There is public opinion! It happened that this judge was a believer in using domestic goods, and he had received an order from the Ministry of Justice to strictly enforce the use of domestic goods, with clear provisions for punishment for those who violated it! After hearing her statement, the judge couldn't help but feel anger rising from his heart, and slammed the table and scolded him, shameless! He had to be imprisoned, and he repented and thought: I didn't expect women to have such magic power! I shouldn't have been so rash..." His wife, seeing that he had a look of repentance, strongly pleaded with the judge to forgive him. The judge agreed! He followed her home in fear and very respectfully!

Several Things Women Should Do During the Women's National Goods Year

— Fei

This year is the Women's National Goods Year. How important is the responsibility that women bear for promoting national goods? Now I put aside all empty talk and only talk about a few things that women in general should do this year.

(1) Regardless of the needs of clothing, food, and housing, make up your mind not to use foreign goods, but only to use domestic goods. Saving one penny on foreign goods is to recover one penny of rights and interests for the country. Beware of saying one thing and doing another, saying that you are promoting national goods on your lips, but in reality, you are a big customer of foreign goods.

(2) Persuade your husband not to use foreign goods. If your husband likes to use foreign goods, you should advise him sternly not to use foreign goods anymore.

(3) If you already have children, then their daily necessities, such as clothes and toys, must not be purchased from foreign goods, and all should be purchased from domestic goods.

(4) Advise relatives and friends to use domestic goods.

What I have said above may be clichés, but if everyone can do so, the effect will definitely be great.

Contribution

Rising Silver Prices and Alarming Trade Deficit Figures

— Yang Mang

Recently, the Jianghai Customs released the international trade situation in this city in January of this year. The trade deficit reached more than 40 million yuan, an unprecedented increase in recent years. Observing the future, there is still a trend of continued surge.

Alarming, this amount of trade deficit is truly enough to control the lives of the Chinese people and plunge them into an abyss of no return. I have tried to investigate the reason, and the main problem lies in the increase in the price of silver in various countries around the world. Since the price of silver is high, it is tantamount to lowering the gold coins of gold-using countries, and the market price of goods in their countries feels even more worthwhile for dumping abroad. China, as a silver-using country, is precisely the most suitable market for various countries to sell goods, and the arrival of foreign goods is like a tide, unstoppable. After this increase, goods abroad are of course worthwhile to import, encroaching on the sales of domestic goods, and the price of domestic goods is implicitly reduced, making it even more difficult to support. This is even more related to the life and death of the future of national goods. Although the alarming trade deficit in January is due to more than one reason, the gift of rising silver prices cannot be denied. In addition, the Chinese people have short-sighted vision and are heavily self-interested, risking impropriety, purchasing Japanese goods and pretending to be domestic goods, and there is no shortage of people who do so. There are even more people who focus on private interests and consider selling Japanese goods as a good plan, regardless of the overall situation. The lack of conscience of people, the shamelessness of people, has reached this point, which is even more painful. We, bearing life and carrying spirit, while one breath still exists, should uphold this conscience to illuminate the treacherous, and also wish patriotic people to rise up together in this Women's National Goods Year to save rights and interests. And the silver price issue should also be thoroughly studied, and jointly seek relief.

Family Talk

Women's National Goods Year and Family Handicrafts

— Zhu Zhenmu

A national goods year has passed, and a women's national goods year has followed. In short, national goods still need to be promoted and manufactured. However, if we look at the national goods factories that have been established, how many are there? Their achievements are already rare! And their capabilities are still insufficient! This is also a matter of fact. Originally, to run a factory perfectly, in addition to huge capital, all aspects such as work management, material allocation, and labor disputes should be paid attention to, and the problem of difficult management, especially in today's China where capital and talent are lacking, feels even more difficult to run a large factory. So, what to do? Just because it's difficult, don't do it? No, in this era of transition from agriculture to industry, since we cannot completely run large factories, then let everyone promote family handicrafts to help the common people and alleviate the urgent need. In this way, in addition to a part of heavy industry being operated by the state, the rest can not require large-scale industry, and can be carried out in the people's homes as units. The capital to run this can be hundreds of yuan, or thousands of yuan. The gathering can be four or five families, or ten or twenty families. If this is the case, I think that farmers living in the unfortunate times of frequent natural disasters may also be able to alleviate their difficulties by engaging in industry in their spare time. It is not known that in addition to promoting national goods, it also solves a part of the rural economy, which is truly achieving two things with one effort.

Isn't there domestically produced woollen goods being manufactured in North China? Those large quantities of woollen goods are not made in coal-burning factories, but are the work results of North China farmers in their spare time. The initiators of this cause were the personnel of the YMCA. Originally, a countless amount of wool was discarded every year in North China, which was an extremely regrettable waste, but since there were no factories, there was no way out without discarding it. The YMCA, seeing this, went to England, the most advanced country in the textile industry, and brought back their simple manual machinery that farmers used to weave wool hundreds of years ago, slightly improved it, and asked carpenters to imitate it, and set up schools to train and teach talents, one to ten, ten to hundreds, and went deep into farmers' families in separate groups, so that rural women could use waste materials and spare time to weave articles. Someone may say high-sounding things like being backward about this kind of old equipment for ten families, but I think this is not shameful, but is a method that is very practicable for China at present. Now the results in North China are like this, as long as you understand it, you will definitely issue a criticism and thought of "Good! Not bad! This is a way!" Since the fact is like this, then all parts of the country can continue to work hard and promote family handicrafts together, which is also the best policy.

The importance of family handicrafts and the need to promote them are as described above, and in this year's so-called women's national goods, promoting family handicrafts is even more timely, because women are the center of gravity of the family, especially in modern China, when women's careers are in a slump, some stay at home, it is better to find another way out, relying on each person's financial resources and abilities, separately or jointly, to run family handicrafts, which seems to be more cost-effective and appropriate. This does not mean that family industry does not need men. In fact, for girls to struggle for equal status, this is truly an extremely flat avenue, and women engaged in family industry can also take care of the responsibilities of housewives in the family at any time, without worrying about him, and can boldly do it. Dear female compatriots: Those of you who see this page of the newspaper are probably intellectual classes who have graduated or studied at some school. Please accept the reporter's intention and transfer the spirit and money you spend on makeup, gambling, or other entertainment every day to the path of engaging in family industry. I think you can receive better happiness than now. This is indeed a major plan that benefits both the public and private and saves the country and the people. Remember! Work hard! Look at this period of the Women's National Goods Year and let the women and the national border release a different light!

Voice of the Telecom World

Telegraph and Roads (Part 2)

— Lü Bing

Although telegraphs are transmitted very quickly, traveling thousands of miles in an instant, there are times when they are somewhat delayed. The reasons for this delay are not just one. If the sender and receiver ask the office counter once, they can fully understand. Now, if someone drives to a certain place and the road in the middle is under repair, temporarily stopping vehicles from coming and going, they have to take a detour to reach their destination. Therefore, the original 15 minutes to reach the destination must be increased by 5 minutes due to the detour. This is a fact that is difficult to avoid, and can also be used as evidence for telegraphs. For example, the Shanghai-Xun (Jiujiang) direct line, occasionally due to disasters that damage the line, one side is repairing it quickly, and at the same time, the transmission of telegraphs cannot but make it slightly delayed. At this time, if the Shanghai-Hankou and Hankou-Xun lines are open, then change to sending to Hankou, and then transfer to Jiujiang. All these dispatches are not uniform. All can be regarded as detours; the time delayed is the time of the detour, and the time spent is very temporary because the circuits are interconnected like blood vessels.

There is usually the so-called "line congestion." This term is also frequently seen in newspapers reporting telegraph news. In fact, line congestion is telegraph congestion. Why does telegraph congestion occur? It can be said that most of it is related to the current situation. When the situation is tense, the telegraphs of the government and army come in droves. Their nature is extremely important and confidential. According to the rules, they should be sent in advance. This is like encountering a fire engine whizzing past on the road, and you have to give way and let it pass first. Also, with so many government and army telegraphs, it is like a transportation hub, with trams, cars, and human-powered vehicles gathered in one place. Drivers must follow the order of priority and cannot arbitrarily increase their speed.

There is also another level, which is the inspection of telegraphs. Usually, telegraphs are not inspected. After simple business procedures, they are sent separately, which is extremely fast. If there is a change in the situation, the military authorities will have an inspection of telegraphs. Once a telegraph is inspected, some inspection time is added in addition to the sending time. During martial law, vehicles passing through are also often stopped everywhere for inspection. If you ask again and again, can the vehicle arrive at the time set in peacetime? The telegraph and the driving car can be equated.

In summary, it can be seen that there are many similarities between road traffic and telegraph traffic; only because road traffic is seen by all, and delays or accidents in driving are considered natural, there is nothing to be surprised about. As for sending telegrams, the transmission situation in the bureau, once exposed, is no different. Those who are clear about roads may not be clear about telegrams. This is because the content of telecommunications has not been announced, and external accusations cannot be avoided. This article of mine may be considered to be defending the people serving in the telecommunications industry. In fact, there are many facts to prove this phenomenon. There is no shortage of enlightened people in all circles. If an investigation is conducted (investigations are very welcome), they will know that the telegraph itself is accurate and fast. Occasionally, there are delays, which are due to various reasons.

"Send a Telegram to Beiping"

— Guan

Reading a report in a Shanghai newspaper, I learned that in the seventh volume of the natural science textbook published by the Great Eastern Book Bureau, there is a lesson called "Send a Telegram to Beiping." The main idea of the content is: "To send a telegram from Shanghai to Beiping, it must be transferred through the Nanjing and Tianjin telegraph bureaus, and it can arrive in one or two days." The Shanghai-Ping telegram must be transferred by Beijing, and it takes another one or two days. Those who have a little telecommunications knowledge cannot help but be horrified when they read it. The author's pen is simply an "amazing pen"!

In fact, this writer, if he must do this lesson "Send a Telegram to Beiping" and is afraid of paying the newspaper fee, may as well take the trouble to go to the telegraph bureau or wireless radio station inquiry office for an inquiry. Building a car behind closed doors can also fit the rut when opening the door. Of course, it will not lead to inaccurate compilation and major mistakes.

However, I have to say again that the writers of textbooks can generally be said to be members of the intellectual class in society, but they have not been able to fully understand telecommunications common sense, so it is even more conceivable for those who are not intellectual class. Therefore, instilling common knowledge of telegraph, telephone, and wireless radio so that everyone can understand and use them is really an "urgent matter."

Establishment of Wired Telegraph Lines in the Past Year (Part 1) by Qian Jiaguang

—

5,371 kilometers of main and branch lines have been repaired.

2,104 kilometers of new lines have been added.

1,093 kilometers of lines have been added to existing poles.

One new underwater cable has been added. Six underwater cables have been repaired and opened. The remaining 22 major sections are currently under repair and reconstruction.

Wired telegraphs have been in China for over fifty years, with a total length of over 100,000 kilometers. Although this is relatively small compared to our area, it is still lagging behind other countries. However, since its inception, it has been affected by politics, local disturbances, and financial difficulties. The establishment of these lines has been severely impacted, which cannot be fully described in a short article. As for the existing lines, they are divided into main lines (幹綫) and branch lines (支綫). Main lines have more communication traffic, so the number of wires is usually greater than that of branch lines. This is also a kind of distinction. The main lines controlled include Hanping (Hankou to Beiping), Huhan (Shanghai to Hankou), Hufu (Shanghai to Fuzhou), Fuguang (Fuzhou to Guangzhou), Jinpu (Tianjin to Pukou), Hanyu (Hankou to Chongqing), Qinghu (Qingdao to Shanghai), Yanji (Yantai to Jinan), Pingqia (Beiping to Qiaqitu), Beining (Beiping to Liaoning), Liaoha (Liaoning to Harbin), Hahei (Harbin to Heihe), Pinglan (Beiping to Lanzhou), Jiuguang (Jiujiang to Guangzhou), Guangyong (Guangzhou to Nanning), Wugui (Wuchang to Guilin), Guinan (Guilin to Nanguan), Changbi (Changsha to Bijie), Xilu (Xi'an to Luzhou), Yudian (Chongqing to Yunnan), Yunxin (Yunnan to Xiaoxinjie), Yunlong (Yunnan to Longzhou), etc. Currently, main line engineering offices have been established in these locations, specifically for maintenance. These include Hanping, Huhan, Hufu, Fuguang, Jinpu, Hanyu, Qinghu, Yanji, Pingqia, and Guangyong. In addition, communication links established between various provinces and cities are generally referred to as branch lines, which are maintained by the respective telegraph offices.

The main components of line construction are wooden poles, wires, wooden crossarms (sometimes not used on branch lines due to fewer wires), and insulators (commonly called porcelain bowls, each with a straight foot or string hook). The lifespan of wooden poles varies depending on the quality of the wood, averaging about six to eight years. With proper maintenance, it may not exceed ten years. Although wires are more durable, they are eroded by wind and rain, and the outer layer tends to rust after being installed for many years, increasing resistance to telegraph communication. Therefore, even if they are not broken, their usable lifespan is only about eighteen years. In addition, the lifespan of wooden crossarms and insulators is even shorter, varying depending on the conditions along the line, and not uniform. Therefore, once a line is built, the daily management and inspection should be thorough. Due to the limited lifespan, in order to ensure good communication, it is necessary to carefully inspect the actual situation and carry out repairs and replacements.

In the past, the maintenance of main and branch lines in China often boasted "minor repairs every three years, major repairs every five years." Major repairs involved completely overhauling the entire line. However, during the era of warlord rule, telegraph facilities were often focused on immediate needs, neglecting the future. Even if the lines exceeded their maintenance lifespan, no preparations were made, and only temporary patching was done. This is like a building that is leaning and leaking, with dangerous signs appearing repeatedly due to procrastination. After the establishment of the National Government's Ministry of Communications, the policy guidelines emphasized line maintenance. Therefore, over the years, except for the impact of banditry or disasters (such as floods and typhoons), the main and branch lines have generally been able to communicate smoothly, even if the line construction was too old. The active efforts to renovate and refresh the lines have also continued without any slackening. In the past year, inquiries to the Ministry of Communications about the establishment of lines have revealed considerable progress. More achievements will be made this year. Lines are an important tool for wired telecommunications, and the simultaneous advancement of repairing old lines and expanding new lines will likely lead to a promising future for communication. Therefore, I have recorded what I have heard as follows.

Repaired Lines

(1) Plan: Surveying the main and branch lines across the country, except for newly established lines, those that have not undergone major repairs have been in service for more than ten years, or at least seven or eight years. Replacing all of them would be uneconomical and financially unsustainable. After considering the situation, a ten-year rotating replacement plan was devised. That is, one-tenth of the rotten poles and wires on the main lines will be replaced each year. In this way, all of them will be replaced within ten years, and the cycle will begin again, which can maintain the lifespan of the lines and meet the annual requirements. As for the branch lines, the urgency is assessed, and the situation is inspected. Old ones are replaced with new ones, aiming for widespread coverage. Although it is not possible to implement the same plan as the main lines, a precise step-by-step plan has been made for provincial-level maintenance.

(2) Statistics: In the past year, the Ministry of Communications repaired a total of 5,371 kilometers of wired telegraph lines. The two categories, main lines and branch lines, are distinguished and listed below.

(A) Main Lines: Total of 3,732 kilometers

Hankou to Jiujiang: 272 kilometers

Shunde to Zhangde: 138 kilometers

Tianjin to Jinan: 348 kilometers

Xuzhou to Pukou: 374 kilometers

Hejigang to Yangxin: 40 kilometers

Qingjiang to Xuzhou, Taizhuang, Lianshui: 421 kilometers

Gaomi to Xinpu: 316 kilometers

Nanjing to Datong: 190 kilometers

Jiujiang to Qianjiangkou: 233 kilometers

Hankou to Guangshui: 161 kilometers

Wuchang to Xianning: 90 kilometers

Yichang to Niukou: 190 kilometers

Beiping to Baoding: 172 kilometers

Wanxian to Liangshan: 104 kilometers

Jinan to Weixian: 207 kilometers

Jiujiang to Wuchang: 269 kilometers

Suzhou to Jiaxing: 92 kilometers

Jiaxing to Chang'an: 61 kilometers

Danyang to Tushanguan: 54 kilometers

(B) Branch Lines: Total of 1,639 kilometers

Badong to Shinan: 202 kilometers

Ouchikou to Wuxizui: 17 kilometers

Shanghai to Gaochangmiao: 11 kilometers

Ankang to Shiquan: 150 kilometers

Hangzhou to Huzhou: 132 kilometers

Nancheng to Nanfeng: 69 kilometers

Zhangzhou to Longyan: 238 kilometers

Nanchang to Fuzhou: 104 kilometers

Xi'an to Tongguan: 139 kilometers

Beiping to Ningyun: 75 kilometers

The above refers specifically to landlines. In addition, the repair of underwater cables in various locations in the 22nd year [of the Republic] included Gaochangmiao to Chuansha, Xiamen to Gulangyu, Yantai to Weihaiwei, and Anqing to Yinjiahui, whether via inland rivers or by sea. Dredging and construction were all completed and restored.

Overview of Step-by-Step Automatic Telephone Exchanges (Continued)

— Jin

Installed at Edwin S. Telephone Exchange

(II) Advantages of Selectors

The selectors of the Strowger automatic telephone exchange have two movements, namely, stepping and rotation. This system only uses one type of rotary selector, each with a total of 102 connection sockets, arranged in a semicircle. Therefore, its parts are interchangeable and easier to maintain, which is more convenient and less troublesome than selectors with two movements. The total weight of the machine is lighter and takes up less space. The time required for wiring, whether local or long-distance, is faster than other types of automatic telephone exchanges, and the sound transmission is also better.

This device itself is also equipped with special equipment that other types do not have. That is, when the telephone traffic is particularly busy, the selectors in areas with simpler traffic can be transferred to areas with particularly busy traffic in a few seconds with simple actions, in order to make adjustments. Therefore, the number of selectors used on weekdays can be reduced.

(III) Advantages of Traffic Recording Equipment

This type of automatic telephone exchange is equipped with an automatic traffic recording meter, which is similar to the one used on the user line, to facilitate the examination of the usage of selectors and the allocation of resources.

(IV) Advantages Regarding Trunk Line Numbers for Small Exchanges

(Note: This refers to the trunk lines used by small exchanges, which require sequential line testing during connection.) Even if the last two digits are zero, it does not matter. Each small exchange group can be expanded at will without changing numbers, and single-number users can also participate.

(V) Regarding the Connection Method between Small Branch Offices

In the same area, if there are several branch offices and the area is not very large, the exchange of users between all neighboring offices is mostly done directly, that is, entirely controlled by the user. However, for small branch offices that are relatively far apart (non-neighboring offices), whose communication lines are relayed through one or more intermediate branch offices, in order to save trunk lines and facilitate route allocation, a "storage" or "translation" equipment is used. Since the number of calls between users in such branch offices is not large, only a few storage or translation devices are needed. Also, if the direct lines to neighboring branch offices are all occupied, the incoming call number can be relayed by the central office. This "Alternative Trunking" can save about one-third of the relay. The bureau can adopt both of these methods. (The End)

Regarding Telegraph Communications in Fuzhou

Reporter

Having read the short commentary "Telegraph Communications in Fuzhou" in the Tianjin Dagongbao on February 6, it roughly stated that the wired telegrams sent by reporters in Fuzhou took seven or eight days to be received, etc. According to personnel from the telegraph side, "The reason for the delay in Fuzhou telegrams is not because the telegraph lines have been damaged and have not been repaired, and must be forwarded via a detour. It is actually because after Chen Mingshu, Li Jishen, and others initiated the rebellion in Fujian, the central government dispatched a large army to Fujian to suppress it. As the army marched, the telegraph offices in various places doubled the amount of reporting, and the Jiangshan-Jian'ou telegraph lines were occupied by two lines by the Transportation Department of the Military Affairs Commission to connect military telephones. As a result, although the Jian'ou, Pucheng, and Hangzhou bureaus have installed high-speed transmitting and receiving machines and added staff, it is still difficult to clear the backlog of telegrams. As for Fuzhou, all the telegraph lines in the north and south have been cut off, and all telegrams can only be relayed by radio, and there is no possibility of transmitting them via a detour. After the wired telegraphs were cut off, the wireless radio alone was responsible for the reporting of both sides, and it was difficult to clear the incoming and outgoing telegrams, so it was inevitable that there would be a backlog. As for the damaged lines along the way after the end of the Fujian incident, they were completely repaired as early as the 24th of last month, but because they are still occupied by the army, the direct Shanghai-Fuzhou work cannot be restored immediately. It was not until the 6th of this month that, after several consultations with the troops stationed along the line, the direct Shanghai-Fuzhou telegraph lines were connected. From then on, Fuzhou telegrams will be transmitted as usual, and there will be no need to worry about backlog," and so on. The reporter notes: Since the Fujian Incident occurred, the first aspect of transportation to be hit was telegraphs. For example, the army cuts off telegraph lines, occupies and borrows telegraph lines, inspects telegrams, and sends many military telegrams, all of which are fatal blows to private telegrams! Therefore, during wartime, it is possible that private telegrams may occasionally be delayed. However, this kind of fact is something that people in the telecommunications industry are extremely willing to avoid.

The Relationship Between the Beijing-Shanghai Long-Distance Telephone and the Press

— Wang Qikun

In the previous issue of this journal, an article by Mr. Ye Zhonghua, "A Discussion on Cooperation Between the Telecommunications Industry and the Press," described the service of the telecommunications industry to the press, and expressed his hope for cooperation between the two. However, the original article only described the situation of telegraphs, without mentioning telephones, so I would like to add a few words to broaden its meaning.

Recently, the press has mostly used long-distance telephones in addition to telegrams to transmit news. Taking Nanjing and Shanghai as an example, the news transmitted by long-distance telephones may not be less than the number of telegrams. The telephone bureau has always paid close attention to the long-distance calls made by newspapers and magazines, and strived to make them convenient; moreover, the news they transmit is not subject to inspection, so there is no delay, which should be well known to the press.

However, due to the small number of telephone lines between Beijing and Shanghai, and the fact that newspapers and magazines use long-distance telephones at the same time, it is inevitable that there will be congestion at times, and it is necessary to change to express calls in order to be scheduled earlier. In addition, the Ministry of Communications has recently stipulated that newspapers and magazines that request cancellation of long-distance calls after they have been connected must pay one-third of the call fee, while ordinary calls do not. The above two matters may still not be fully satisfactory to the press. In view of this, the Ministry of Communications decided last year to set up four pairs of direct long-distance telephone lines along the Beijing-Shanghai highway, which can be used as six pairs. Construction has started and will be completed in three or four months. At that time, newspapers and magazines can make calls at any time without having to rush in advance. As for the cancellation of long-distance calls after they have been connected, it has now been changed to treat newspapers and magazines the same as ordinary users, and a fixed date has been set for implementation. Moreover, after the completion of the new telephone lines between Beijing and Shanghai, calls will be smooth and will not be affected by excessive registration, so the temporary cancellation can be reduced.

According to the operating statistics of long-distance telephones between Beijing and Shanghai over the years, adding one pair of telephone lines to the existing telephone lines is enough to cope with everything; now suddenly adding as many as six pairs, costing five or six hundred thousand yuan, the purpose can be said to be entirely for the convenience of the press. From this, we can also see the spirit of service of the telecommunications industry to the press.

National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph

— Xu Yinlu

Chinese characters are complex and have many parts. They are not as simple as English, which uses only 26 letters to form different words and sentences. Therefore, in telegraph transmission, it is necessary to use a legal code to represent each character, that is, the so-called four-character code. Before a telegram is transmitted, the message must first be translated into a four-character code, and the receiving station then translates the four-character code into Chinese. Speed is essential for telegrams, and such translation is too uneconomical in terms of time and very troublesome in terms of procedures. Therefore, public telegrams sent by railways, ships, and telecommunications organizations mostly use English for the sake of speed and convenience. However, it must be said to be a kind of shame and embarrassment for our country, which claims to have a cultural history of several thousand years, to use English to send telegrams to ourselves!

Using English does not respect the national system, and using the four-character code has the trouble of double translation, so the wave of reforming my country's telegrams is swelling day by day. However, the basic condition for reforming telegrams is to create another kind of telegram that can be understood at a glance without translation. After a long period of research, the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph was produced in this brewing sound!

The so-called National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph is a telegram that is sent and received using the legal symbols to represent the phonetic alphabet. The sender only needs to write the phonetic alphabet, and the receiver knows the meaning of the text by reading the pronunciation. The procedures are simple, and the time is saved. When telegraphers have questions about receiving and sending, they can immediately ask on the machine, reducing errors. There is also a kind of National Phonetic Alphabet abbreviation to represent fixed names or idioms, in order to save the number of telegrams, such as "National Government" (國民政府) only needs to write　　　　, "Because of this order" (等因奉此)　　　　. If you specialize in using nouns with the same sound and different meanings or obscure words and sentences, you must first use pronunciation to adjust it. There are a total of one pronunciation: Yin, Yang, Ping, Shang, Qu, Ru. If the cut sound is not accurate, the word will be read differently. Then use the transmission department to distinguish the department affiliation of the word. There are a total of 102 transmission departments, dividing the various departments, which is easier to remember than the four-character code. For example, the word "electricity" (電); the National Phonetic Alphabet is "　｜　　｜　", "　｜　" is the pronunciation of the word electricity. "　" is the pronunciation, indicating that it is the Qu sound "　　" is the transmission department, representing that it is the Yu character department. Although a word requires six phonetic symbols to replace it, the words used in the pronunciation department are few, so we only need to memorize the pronunciation and transmission department, and any word can be solved! Before memorizing and generalizing, you can also check the "National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph Compilation" compiled by the former Ministry of Communications Pinyin Research Association.

Telegrams sent abroad also have a kind of National Phonetic Alphabet Roman alphabet telegraph, which uses Roman characters to replace the National Phonetic Alphabet, and the organization is very sound. In addition, the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph also bears a major mission, which is to promote language unity! Promote cultural progress!

Anything will be more difficult when it is first started, and the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph is of course no exception. However, we must put aside personal interests and feelings, and think purely rationally for the sake of society, and we can immediately think of the need for active promotion and universality!

The National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph must first be promoted by our colleagues in the telecommunications industry. This is of course the case, but if the society is confused, the effect is still zero, so on the one hand, we must start the trial from the telecommunications industry, and on the other hand, we must actively publicize it and apply it to the society.

Now I will introduce the progress of the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph in the railway sector: Before the 11th year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Communications held the Fourth Transportation Conference in Beiping. Mr. Tan Yaozong, the representative of the Sidao Railway and the inventor of the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph, proposed that the railway telegrams should be changed to the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph. The resolution was that the Sidao Railway should conduct a trial first. In July of the 14th year, the Sidao Railway completed its reform mission. After a three-year trial period, it was repeatedly obstructed and experienced many twists and turns, but enthusiasm and perseverance finally achieved the final victory.

Since the reform of the Sidao Railway was successful, the railways in the Northeast followed suit, and soon all were completely successful. Now all the railways in the Northeast uniformly use the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph, and they all feel that it is much more convenient than foreign languages and the four-character code. (It is said that after the September 18th Incident, the railways in the Northeast were forced to use Japanese telegrams. If this is true, the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegrams that have been painstakingly operated by the railways in the Northeast for several years will be completely destroyed.)

In March of the 19th year, the Ministry of Railways, in order to respect the national system, first ordered all railways across the country to use Chinese for all road use texts. Regarding railway telegrams, it was also decided to change to the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph in accordance with the precedent of the Northeast railways. Therefore, two Northeast National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph experts were hired to establish a National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph training class in the ministry. Officials from the ministry and Beijing-Shanghai, Tianjin-Pukou, Jiaoji, Xiang-E, and Nan-Xun railways were sent to attend the research. The graduates of the two phases were very successful, and the graduates were sent back to the road to promote the class teaching one after another, and the Beijing-Shanghai Tianjin-Pukou and the Ministry of Railways began to use the National Phonetic Alphabet for telegrams. It has been three years since then, and the effect is quite good. Subsequently, the Longhai Road Qing and other roads have also been taught. Now the Tianjin-Pukou and Beijing-Shanghai roads are actively promoting the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph Promotion Committee in order to complete the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph as soon as possible. We believe that in the near future, the railway telegrams will be completely National Phonetic Alphabet.

Scientific inventions progress with social needs, everything new replaces the old, and the perfect eliminates the unhealthy. Don't we think that using English telegrams is inappropriate? Don't we feel that using four-character code telegrams is inconvenient? Then we must actively reform. Reform must be the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph! We must complete the mission of reform as soon as possible; our colleagues in the telecommunications industry must work together!

Editor's Note: Regarding the promotion of the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph, the National Phonetic Alphabet Telegraph Compilation compiled and printed by the former Ministry of Communications in the 20th year of the Republic of China differs greatly from the current new standard of phonetic symbols of the Central Government. The Central Government has already sent personnel to revise it, and has taken the original manuscript to the National Language Unification Preparatory Committee in Beiping for detailed review. It is said that the compilation will be finalized soon, and work can be started.

Semi-Monthly News

— Community Member

Postal and Telegraph Bureaus to Implement Joint Establishment

In order to facilitate public communications and save expenses, the Ministry of Communications recently ordered the General Post Office to send personnel to Beijing to discuss the joint establishment of postal and telegraph bureaus with the Telecommunications Department of the ministry, and ordered the relevant postal and telegraph bureaus to expedite the joint establishment in accordance with the plan. The main points of the plan are outlined below:

(1) Third-class and lower-class telegraph bureaus should be jointly established with post offices in one location, starting with a trial in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hebei provinces.

(2) For post offices with branches in major commercial ports, the telegraph bureau may set up receiving stations in the post office branches. For telegraph bureaus with receiving and sending branches, the post office may set up post office branches in each location. However, the business hours will still be in accordance with the business hours of the bureau where they are located.

(3) In major commercial ports where the Ministry of Communications has established city or long-distance telephones, the telephone bureau may install public telephones in each post office.

(4) In places where a telegraph bureau has been established but no post office has yet been established, a postal agency may be set up in the telegraph bureau, and the telegraph bureau will act as an agent for postal services.

(5) In places where postal and telegraph bureaus have not yet been jointly established, the telegraph bureau and the telephone bureau should sell stamps and receive and send ordinary letters.

The above plan will be implemented in succession in about two months. After that, public communications in various places will be greatly facilitated.

Railway Telegrams Exempted from Additional Line Fees

The railway station's collection and transfer of telegrams was originally set up to facilitate communication for the public in places where there are no telegraph bureaus but there are stations. However, in addition to charging according to the telegraph bureau's price list, each word of this railway line's transferred telegram must also be charged an additional line fee of two cents, which seems to be a burden on the sender. It is now heard that the Ministry of Communications, in order to thoroughly facilitate the public and develop the railway telegram business, has decided that from March 1, the additional line fee that has been charged will be announced to all telegraph bureaus, and the Railway Department will be requested to forward it to all stations, so that all stations will be exempted, so that the fees are the same as those of the telegraph bureaus.

Postal Transfer Telegrams Exempted from Postage

The Ministry of Communications recently stated that postal transfer telegrams were originally set up to facilitate public communication in places where telegraph bureaus are not set up, and that the original postage of 25 cents per telegram should be exempted so that the public in remote cities can enjoy the same benefits as the public in large cities. It is heard that the Ministry of Communications has decided that from March 15, the post office and the telegraph bureau will implement this exemption of postage.

Bureau and Station Telegram Envelopes Pre-Printed

Telegraph bureaus and stations with busy reporting services often receive more than 1,000 or hundreds of telegrams per day. If the envelopes for the telegrams are written at any time, the reporting of each telegram will inevitably be delayed. In order to improve business, the Ministry of Communications has now ordered busy bureaus and stations to pre-print or write a large number of telegram envelopes for merchants or residents who receive a lot of telegrams. They are placed in a specially made telegram envelope rack for each household, so that they can be taken out and used at any time. After this method is implemented, the delivery of telegrams will be even faster.

Yarn and Flowers Rong Yarn New Standard Golden Rooster Listed

Issued with Lightning Speed

Bidding Produces Minor Disturbances

Bidding Process

The issue of changing the standard yarn, which has been debated for a long time, to the Golden Rooster was originally scheduled to be put up for auction on March 1. However, it was feared that the scheduled announcement would cause obstacles. Therefore, the means of lightning speed was used, and it was suddenly put up for auction one day early yesterday (February 28). The five, six, seven, and three-month periods were operated simultaneously. According to brokers, they had not received notification beforehand, so the market situation was chaotic before the market opened in the morning. Among them, there were still dozens of households who opposed changing the standard, and they were temporarily watching the new standard. In the afternoon, brokers convened an emergency meeting to discuss countermeasures, which were roughly still to mediate and cooperate.

Yesterday, the yarn market trend was initially down and then back up, and the situation was still calm. Silk and Tea: Overseas Silk Sales Difficult to Revive

(Inventory of Second-Grade Foreign Warehouses is Dwindling) The foreign firms in this port dealing in Chinese silk exports, recognizing that Japanese silk is being dumped at low prices in overseas markets and that Chinese silk prices are still difficult to stabilize, are unwilling to take risks by stockpiling existing silk. Since the beginning of winter last year, European and American firms have lacked large-scale purchases of forward silk, adhering to the principle of buying and shipping as needed. Therefore, the inventory of silk in foreign warehouses is dwindling. Yesterday, at the end of February, a field investigation was conducted at the silk warehouses of various foreign firms, and it was found that the total inventory of factory white, yellow, and gray silks was less than 800 bales, of which 235 bales were prepared for shipment to the Americas, 353 bales to Europe, and 190 bales to Asia.

(The Amount of Zhe Silk Transported to Shanghai is Decreasing Daily) Since the invasion of Japanese silk, the American sales of the compound-reeled silks produced in Zhejiang and Hunan (i.e., Ji Silk) have almost disappeared. As a result, most silk firms in the Xum (Nanxun) and Zhen (Zhenze) producing areas have suspended operations, and silk production is decreasing daily. Only a total of 247 bales of lower-grade dry reeled silk were shipped to Shanghai last month to meet the demands of Indochina firm (i.e., White Head foreign firm).

Hardware: Ribbed Steel Bars Sell Actively

Ribbed steel bars have recently been selling very actively, so the daily opening quantity has been as high as sixty or seventy tons. Transactions by construction groups on this street have also been quite brisk. In the past few days, orders have been placed for more than two hundred tons. The price for 2-fen material is 130 yuan per ton, and for 3-fen material, it is 127 yuan 5 jiao. Square material is generally estimated at 112 yuan, which is an improvement compared to before. It is said that overseas quotations have been gradually rising in recent days, so the market in this port may not easily decline in the short term.

Free Talk

Not Knowing Its Taste

— Dun Pang

A few days ago, Mr. Bai Yan talked about cormorants, saying that although they chase fish to serve their masters, they rarely get their fill. This reminded me of a story in "A New Account of Tales of the World":

"When Gu Rong was in Luoyang, he once attended a feast. He noticed that the barbecue chef had a longing look on his face for the roasted meat, so he stopped eating his portion and gave it to him. The others at the table laughed at him. Gu Rong said, 'How can there be someone who handles it all day long and does not know its taste?' Later, when chaos broke out and he crossed the Yangtze River, there was always someone by his side in times of danger. When asked why, it was the man who had received the roasted meat."

"Handling it all day long without knowing its taste" can also be used as a comment on cormorants. It turns out that there are such animals in the world, and there are such humans, but Gu Rong adds a "How can there be" at the beginning and a "eh" at the end, making a fuss and showing only his limited insight.

A Tang Dynasty poem about bees says, "After gathering hundreds of flowers to make honey, for whom is the hard work, for whom the busy effort?" This is also a metaphor for people who labor without enjoyment. However, human laborers are definitely not comparable to cormorants and bees.

I have also seen cormorants. Although they rarely get their fill before catching fish, they do get their fill when their work is done. At that time, they and the fishermen are content, lined up on both sides of the bamboo raft, shaking their feathers, chattering "Gaa! Gaa!" and enjoying the pleasure of rest. After returning home, the master does not ask them to do other work, and they have no worries about life, so they are actually very happy.

As for bees, just watching them laboring all day long while humming poems "Buzz! Buzz!" is like a group of "Tao Yuanming"-style "farmers." Although their products are exploited, they are not in a state of slavery in other aspects.

Moreover, cormorants in relation to fish, and bees in relation to honey, cannot be said to "not know its taste" after all; even in a state of exploitation, they can still taste a part of it. If the dragon liver, phoenix marrow, delicacies from land and sea enjoyed by the nobles, those who are hired as 'boys' truly get nothing. Therefore, the barbecue chef, having received a meal from Gu Rong, was endlessly grateful.

Gu Rong's words are just the silly words of an ignorant aristocrat, but they are also a question that cannot be answered even today.

Reading Notes

— Yuan Che

'Spare my life!'

Their voices were shrill. Most of them were young.

They jumped into the shell hole and crouched down. Some of our brothers went to the edge of the hole and shot at the huddled Germans. Many tightly clasped hands stretched out from the chimney-shaped grave, begging for mercy. But no one had any pity. The brothers shot at the hole...

The above passage is copied from Harrison's article "The General Died in Bed." Reading it made me extremely excited and reminded me of another similar but more tragic and terrifying thing. It was when I was a child that I heard it from my maternal uncle. He himself started as a soldier and went through many wars before becoming a company commander, "and his life was lost in the battle of Longquanyi when the Yunnan army approached Chengdu. Although he has been dead for more than ten years, his childlike, playful manner is still preserved in my memory. When he came back on leave, he would line me and other children up at my grandmother's house, shouting 'Turn left,' 'Turn right,' 'Lie down, the enemy is coming,' making such an interesting game of military exercises. This made me happy to pester him all day long, even when he was telling my grandmother and aunts stories about the battlefield, I would lie across his lap, listening while scratching his hands and chin. It was in such a scene that I heard the tragedy of the massacre of prisoners, which I could not forget.

At that time, whenever he mentioned the Yunnan army, he was very angry. He didn't call them the Yunnan army, he just called them "Yunnan brats" (although it is three characters, it should be pronounced as two syllables, "brats" must be read together), because, according to him, whenever "Yunnan brats" caught any of their brothers, they would always stab them to death with bayonets, without any mercy. So they treated the disarmed Yunnan army with even more cruel and vicious methods to vent their hatred. He said that once on the front line, many Yunnan soldiers were surrounded. They did not care how pitifully those poor people begged for mercy, but frantically stabbed at their mouths, eyes, and stomachs with bayonets. Later, they felt that it was still not satisfying, so someone suggested tying the remaining frightened prisoners upside down on trees with ropes, hanging them high in the air. Then one person climbed up the tree, took a knife, dug out the prisoner's intestines from his anus, tied them to a branch, and immediately released the rope holding him up. Then the prisoner's body would fall down slowly, and the bloody intestines would hang in the air like a rope. The prisoner died with strange wails and in a terribly tragic way. Everyone's heart of revenge was then happily satisfied. My uncle shook his head when he spoke of this, saying that it was too cruel. My grandmother, mother, and aunts were so frightened that they trembled, chanting "Amitabha" repeatedly. Comparing this with what Harrison wrote, the Chinese were undoubtedly more advanced than the foreign devils in terms of cruelty. Such a massacre of prisoners was just a small matter.

Two Suicides

— Ren Baige

Not long ago, Mr. Zhu Xiang suddenly committed suicide. His suicide as a poet and university professor should have caused a bit of a stir in society, in reason. However, the result disappeared lightly, just like a pebble thrown into the sea. Recently, Ms. Ai Xia also committed suicide in the midst of the firecracker noises when everyone was gathering happily with their families. According to social custom, her suicide as a woman and a star could have caused a sensation like that of Huang Huiru and Huang Baiying. However, this news has already left us as quickly as the Lunar New Year. Perhaps the event itself lacked the interest of a story. From this, we can know to what extent society has become numb, and people's suicides have become a commonplace event that no longer surprises.

However, the suicides of Mr. Zhu Xiang and others, especially when two such different types of people each embark on the same path from different starting points, is still a social problem worth considering, and we who live in society should think deeply about it.

I don't know much about Mr. Zhu Xiang's life. However, since I saw his article "On Writing" in "Literature," I have been a little worried about him. Because such a mystical view of art for art's sake inevitably leads to either consciously harming others or unconsciously ruining oneself. I am also not very clear about Ms. Ai Xia's life, but according to many friends, she was a relatively progressive woman who had struggled with society, so it was completely unexpected that she would finally desert from the arduous path of life.

It is said that Mr. Zhu Xiang's suicide was mainly due to unemployment; Ms. Ai Xia's suicide was mainly due to heartbreak. Unemployment and heartbreak are originally the source of two major pains in life, but there is no other way besides suicide. And in fact, there are still a large number of unemployed and heartbroken people living. Therefore, their suicides should naturally be the responsibility of society, but further explanation cannot but be sought from themselves. Mr. Zhu Xiang was a poet, and a genius poet praised in his environment. It is certainly valuable to be a poet with genius, but if one thinks of oneself as a genius, feels that one's every word and deed is the law and truth of the universe and society, the result will be to detach oneself from society and people and go to another uninhabited world, and a world very far from society and people is "death." Ms. Ai Xia may have thought herself very clever, at least the kind of environment in which only people buy her goodwill would not make her believe that she was not clever. Naturally, she could walk those unfamiliar roads with her eyes on the sky, carelessly. Walking in this way often leads to slopes and even cliffs, and finally falling to one's death. A clever woman originally has a very good future, but the greatest danger is that the cleverness is flaunted so self-importantly that it turns into something that destroys herself. Because in the midst of flaunting cleverness, she can easily cause others to lose themselves, and also easily cause herself to lose others, and the result is often to lose herself at the same time. This is a worldly wisdom that I have seen too much of, and I only hope that Ms. Ai Xia was not like this!

There is no need to say anything that is close to blame. They can be said to have taken out their last lives to show their kind hearts that would not kill others but would only commit suicide. They did not borrow the lives of others to continue their own lives.

Suicide is cowardly and brave, worthy of condemnation and worthy of sympathy. From the perspective of society, although a person has his own life, he does not exist for himself alone. The universe is constantly growing, the earth is constantly moving, and people are the offspring that protect their lives. A person must not fail to take responsibility for human society. Society is too dark, and we should strive to make it bright; humanity is too terrible, and we should strive to improve it. Even if one has to die, at a minimum, one should make those who create darkness and terror die before oneself. In the gamble of life, is death not the greatest capital? Therefore, a person's suicide is cowardly and worthy of condemnation. But if we look at it from the perspective of individual virtue, it is sometimes brave and worthy of sympathy. Suicide itself requires the greatest courage, at least it shows that one cannot live in a compromising and opportunistic way. What does it mean to live quietly and die quietly? Furthermore, not everyone lives meaningfully: some people live for survival and for meaning, that is, they live meaningfully and strive for meaningful survival, and finally even abandon their own survival to strive for meaning; others live only for survival and not for meaning, even destroying all meaning and living sinfully. For a person who cannot strive for meaningful survival or live meaningfully, but does not attempt to live sinfully, in a passive way, suicide may not be a good way for them to deal with themselves, and this can contain countless sorrows and pains. Moreover, when the freedom to die is deprived from ordinary people, their actions of disposing of their own lives and deaths with full freedom may be felt as a kind of resistance and satisfaction by themselves. What else can we break away from? However, this ultimately lacks a bit of tragic grandeur, that is, dying is not tragic enough.

As mentioned earlier, although Mr. Zhu Xiang and Ms. Ai Xia both walked the path of suicide, their starting points were completely different; one can be said to be one who cannot, and perhaps does not want, to eat people in the old, and one can be said to be one who has not, and perhaps does not want, to endure hardship in the new, so one committed suicide because of resentment at not being recognized, and the other committed suicide because of a lack of fighting spirit. Needless to say, from this we can see the inevitable fate of those who cannot make a sudden turn in the struggle between the old and the new, and Mr. Zhu Xiang and Ms. Ai Xia are just two victims standing at the forefront.

In today's society, killing is going on every day, and in fact, there are many suicides. It is not limited to Mr. Zhu Xiang and Ms. Ai Xia! However, the customs of general society only see the things that float on the surface. I cannot avoid being vulgar, so I will only mention them to express my opinion.

Buddhist Seal Lake

— Bai Yan

These past few days my heart has been quite restless, and I often like to meditate when I have nothing to do. Especially the Buddhist Seal Lake in my hometown: the verdant mountain scenery and the clear blue water deeply evoke my nostalgia at all times.

When I was at home, whenever I felt distressed, I would often invite two or three friends to take a stroll there. Walking slowly under the shade of the trees along the flat lakeside road. Smelling the fragrance of unknown herbs, and seeing the brilliant wild flowers exuding fat calyxes, I felt very happy in my heart.

Sometimes, I would climb to the top of the mountain to look out over the wilderness, seeing the well-like fields, the undulating green waves of rice, and the corner of a red wall of a temple hidden in the green trees, just like reading a rhythmic prose poem. I often lingered there for a very long time, and could not bear to go back.

During the Qingming Festival, the tombs on the mountains on both sides fluttered with ribbon-like white paper. Looking from a distance, they looked like powder butterflies flying in the grass. Sometimes, countless black dots of kites were nailed in the blue sky, quite like the stars in the summer evening. When the weather was gloomy, the mournful cries of widows flowed out of the mountain hollows, and the gentle and dying sound rippled on the lake, adding countless desolations to this quiet lake and mountain.

In summer, the scorching sun shone on the ground like fire. But under the willows of the Buddhist Seal Lake, it was still very cool. At this time, you could see many tea drinkers occupying a seat under the willows leaning against the mountain and water, slowly sipping tea, and lazily talking idly.

When I was suffering from the heat, I often liked to run to this place. First, I would brew a pot of tea at the lakeside tea house, and then occupy a small table under the willows. I would change my position as the shadow of the sun moved.

The drooping willows by the water gently fanned the breeze; the fish in the lake talked to the algae. In this quiet scene, listening to the lonely cicadas chirping, the feeling of "wealth and honor are floating clouds" could not help but arise in my heart.

Sometimes, even if the weather was not very hot, I often liked to run to this place. Facing a pot of tea, I meditated peacefully; sitting alone for most of the day. Although I have no such addiction to tasting tea.

The Diary of Mary Machinaff (IV) by Stephen Leacock

— Translated by Ye Zi

Five days later - Oddo and I do not want to die! We shall escape together, by the time Alexis comes, we are already far away. However, Oddo told me that it is not good to leave empty-handed. Therefore, I give a parcel to my knight everyday, telling him to put these parcels in his hotel. The day before yesterday, I gave him a jewellery box. Yesterday, listening to him, I withdrew the savings from the bank, today, he cleverly told me to steal the keepsakes of my father and mother… Therefore, tonight, I intend to take my father’s gold watch whilst he is asleep… By tomorrow, Oddo and I, the two of us will leave this place forever.

X X X X X X X X X

The following night - my heart is broken! The thing that I feared suddenly happened; … Alexis has arrived. He and Oddo are fighting! … It looks really scary!... Oddo and I were in the pasture, suddenly, Alexis appeared, his stature was originally tall, and his momentum was very fierce. I shouted:

“Oddo! I love… Let’s go… do not kill him!”

Oddo hesitated for a moment and then escaped… How noble he escaped! However, Alexis chased him. They then fought! … Ah! What a scary sight! … Alexis grabbed Oddo’s waist, tossing him around like a stone.

His pants tore; Oddo fell on the grass; Alexis kicked him, then dragged him up, and pressed a wooden yoke onto his shoulders. Then, lifting his butt, threw him into the river. My poor Oddo began to struggle in the river, his head sticking out of the yoke.

Suddenly, Alexis turned around and walked towards me, held me, and brought me back to my house, muttering sweet words…

This is really killing me! I am going to marry Alexis, at the same time, the situation of that poor Oddo, intrudes into my imagination. I thought of him struggling in the water with a wooden yoke. The river will take him to the Dnieper, to the Bug, to the Volga, and then to the Caspian Sea. But that Caspian Sea is not connected to other seas, so maybe Oddo will roll around in it… My heart is broken. I want to cry. (The End)
